| 263 | Class C for $\beta\gamma$ or $bc$ is witnessed by the internal weight-changing line or by an unspecified charged stratum. | The $\beta\gamma$/$bc$ families do realize class C, and the weight-changing slice is a real computed locus. | Conflates a one-dimensional internal slice, where the shadow tower vanishes, with the actual family-level class-C witness. | The weight-changing line is shadow-trivial: $\Theta^{\le r}\vert_{\mathrm{w.c.}}=0$ for $r\ge2$. The class-C witness is the standard conformal-weight family $\beta\gamma_\lambda$ or $bc_\lambda$, with $S_2=6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1$, $S_3=0$, $S_4=-5/12$, and $S_r=0$ for $r\ge5$. | slice/family conflation |
| 264 | Bare `d(Vir)=3` or `d_{\mathrm{alg}}(\mathrm{Vir})=3`. | Virasoro does have a genuine depth-3 invariant in the Gelfand-Fuchs/generating sense. | Conflates generating depth with algebraic shadow depth. | The correct split is $d_{\mathrm{gen}}(\mathrm{Vir})=3$ and $d_{\mathrm{alg}}(\mathrm{Vir})=\infty$. Every Virasoro depth claim must name the depth invariant explicitly. | invariant conflation |
| 265 | Class C requires a `stratum separation` mechanism to add one extra finite level beyond the discriminant dichotomy. | The finite quartic witness and the impossibility of algebraic depth 3 are both real. | Replaces the first-principles depth-gap statement by an unsupported narration about charged sectors. | `prop:depth-gap-trichotomy` gives the correct finite possibilities: $d_{\mathrm{alg}}\in\{0,1,2,\infty\}$. The class-C case is the standard conformal-weight family with $S_3=0$, $S_4=-5/12$, $S_r=0$ for $r\ge5$; there is no separate finite depth-3 stage to be created by narration. | mechanism error |
| 266 | `\cite{Hinich2001}` names a live local bibliography item for the Hinich rectification remark. | A plausible bibkey automatically resolves to the intended canonical source, so the citation still grounds the sentence. | `chapters/theory/theorem_C_refinements_platonic.tex` cites `Hinich2001`, but `bibliography/references.tex` has only `HS87`, `HS93`, and `Hin97`; there is no `Hinich2001` entry, so the build produces `[?]` and the proof trail disappears. | Every cite key must match a live canonical alias in the bibliography. | 267 | `GR17` may be described in prose as `Francis--Gaitsgory`. | Any nearby Gaitsgory-adjacent source can be named from memory without checking the bibliography entry behind the key. | In `chapters/theory/theorem_C_refinements_platonic.tex`, the prose attribution says `Francis--Gaitsgory`, but `bibliography/references.tex` defines `GR17` as D. | 268 | Finite-dimensional bar cohomology at each conformal weight is enough to discharge `lem:perfectness-criterion` and prove family perfectness. | Weightwise finiteness automatically upgrades to the total finite-dimensional flat fiber cohomology required by the perfectness lemma. | The proof of `prop:perfectness-standard-landscape` ends with `finite-dimensional at each conformal weight` / `finite graded dimension at each conformal weight`, while `lem:perfectness-criterion` requires total finite-dimensional flat fiber cohomology after the spectral sequence collapses to degree $0$. Infinitely many nonzero weights can still make the total fiber infinite-dimensional. | To invoke `lem:perfectness-criterion`, the proof must supply the missing bridge to total finite-dimensional degree-$0$ fiber cohomology, or else weaken the proposition to the weightwise statement it actually proves. Weightwise control alone is strictly weaker than total finiteness. | weaker-than-required proof discharge |
| 269 | The chiral bar-cobar adjunction $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} \dashv B^{\mathrm{ch}}$ holds at chain level (Theorem A stated without homotopical qualifier). | There is a bar-cobar adjunction of the right general form between chiral cobar and chiral bar, after suitable homotopical refinement. | Bar-cobar pairs in the filtered/chiral setting almost never give strict chain-level adjunctions: the counit $\epsilon: \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} B^{\mathrm{ch}} A \to A$ and the unit $\eta: C \to B^{\mathrm{ch}} \Omega^{\mathrm{ch}} C$ require a coalgebra-splitting of the bar filtration that exists only up to coherent homotopy. The triangle identities hold on the nose only after passing to the homotopy category or to ind-completion. | State Theorem A as an adjunction of $(\infty,1)$-categories (or of the associated derived/homotopy categories), not as a strict chain-level adjunction. Every "adjunction" claim in the programme must specify one of: (i) strict chain-level (rare — needs explicit splitting witness), (ii) homotopy-category / derived-category level, (iii) $(\infty,1)$-categorical. The chiral version is (ii)/(iii), not (i). | adjunction-strictness conflation |
| 270 | "Every standard chiral algebra reduces, under the averaging map $\mathrm{av}: \mathfrak{g}^{E_1} \to \mathfrak{g}^{\mathrm{mod}}$, to one of the four archetypes G / L / C / M." | The four archetypes (Heisenberg, affine Kac-Moody, $\beta\gamma$, Virasoro) do exhaust a precisely delimitable class of chiral algebras. | The word "standard" silently carries the scope hypothesis. Without a definition of "standard chiral algebra" (Koszul $E_1$-chiral? Finitely strongly generated? Freely generated? Affine-type?), the dichotomy silently excludes parafermions $\mathbb{Z}_k$, $\mathcal{W}_N$ at general $N$, coset VOAs, non-unimodular lattice VOAs, triplet / symplectic fermion, and logarithmic extensions — each of which can fail to fit the four-archetype classification. | Classification claims must name the hypothesis class under which exhaustiveness is proved (candidate: finitely strongly generated Koszul $E_1$-chiral algebras over a smooth curve, admitting a conformal vector). Handle the non-standard examples in a separate remark listing which archetypes they realize (or fail to realize). The dichotomy is a theorem about a class, not about "all chiral algebras". | classification-scope silently unstated |
| 271 | $r_{\max}(A)$ (shadow-tower depth / algebraic depth $d_{\mathrm{alg}}(A)$) is invoked as an invariant of the chiral algebra $A$ without a separate proposition establishing presentation-independence. | Depth is a real, well-defined invariant on an appropriate class of chiral algebras; Theorem D (obstruction-tower universality $\mathrm{obs}_g = \kappa \cdot \lambda_g$) rests on depth being a property of $A$, not of a chosen presentation. | Without a presentation-independence proposition, $r_{\max}$ is at most an invariant of the strong-generation set. Any classification theorem or universality statement that treats $r_{\max}(A)$ as algebra-level data is incomplete until presentation-independence is proved; drift here propagates silently from Theorem D to every numerical consequence. | Depth invariants must be paired with a presentation-independence proposition. Either (a) exhibit a canonical strong generating set stable under chiral automorphisms and prove $r_{\max}$ is computed on it, or (b) define $r_{\max}(A) := \inf_{\text{presentations}} r_{\max}$ and prove the infimum is attained. State and label the independence result separately (e.g., `prop:depth-presentation-independence`). | invariant vs presentation conflation |
| 272 | "The conformal vector $\omega$ kills the chiral direction, promoting $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ from $E_2$ to $E_3$." (Or analogous: "$X$ kills $Y$", "$X$ forces the transition", "$X$ promotes $E_n$ to $E_{n+1}$".) | Conformal-vector-driven topologization is a real mechanism; Deligne-style $E_n$ promotion by a chosen distinguished element (Hoch$^*(A) = E_2$ + conformal vector $\to E_3$) is classical. | "Kills the chiral direction" is narrative, not a chain-level operation. The conformal vector $\omega$ is a distinguished element of $A$, not an operator on $B(A)$ or on $C^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(A,A)$. Without exhibiting the explicit chain homotopy $h_\omega$ satisfying $[d, h_\omega] = \mathrm{id} - p_{\mathrm{top}}$ (projection onto the topological sector), or the explicit $E_3$-operad action built from $\omega$, the topologization step is unmathematized narration. | Every "X kills Y" / "X promotes $E_n$ to $E_{n+1}$" / "X forces the transition" claim must expose: (i) the chain-level map (chain homotopy, Koszul contraction, or operad-valued morphism) that does the killing/promoting, (ii) the homotopy identity it satisfies ($dh + hd = \mathrm{id} - p$ or equivalent), (iii) a check that the resulting operation assembles into an action of the claimed operad on the correct derived-centre pair. Otherwise restate as conjecture or heuristic. | narration as mechanism (chain-level map missing) |
| 273 | $\Phi: \mathrm{CY}_d\text{-categories} \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X$ is called a "functor" (Vol III central construction). | There is a systematic construction attaching a chiral algebra to each CY-d category in a suitable class; the object-level correspondence is real and productive. | Without a morphism-preservation theorem — does a CY functor $F: \mathcal{C} \to \mathcal{D}$ produce a chiral morphism $\Phi(F): \Phi(\mathcal{C}) \to \Phi(\mathcal{D})$? — $\Phi$ is an object-level correspondence, not a functor. Morphisms of CY-d categories (cyclic $A_\infty$ functors, shifted-Lagrangian correspondences, trace-preserving exact functors) do not obviously descend to chiral-algebra morphisms without an explicit bimodule / Maurer-Cartan-transport step. Different CY-morphism classes give different target morphism classes. | State $\Phi$ as an object-level construction unless morphism-preservation is proved and inscribed. If proved, name the source morphism class explicitly and construct $\Phi(F)$ via a named mechanism (defect bimodule, MC transport, deformation-quantization modular-operad map). In Vol III, audit every use of "$\Phi$ is a functor" against this standard; where morphism-preservation is not established, downgrade to "object-level correspondence" or "assignment". | functor vs object-level correspondence conflation |
| 274 | $\langle \Lambda | \Lambda \rangle = c(5c+22)/10$ (Zamolodchikov norm) or $S_4 = 10/[c(5c+22)]$ imported by citation to Zamolodchikov / BPZ. | The identity is correct and well-attested in the physics literature under standard conventions. | Cited numerical identities with convention-dependent factors (OPE coefficients, mode conventions, Virasoro-primary orthogonalization coefficient $3/10$, normalization of $T$) silently import the source's convention stack. A programme with first-principles epistemic standards cannot rely on citation for load-bearing constants that appear in $\kappa$ per family, shadow tower $S_k$, or derived-centre complementarity $\kappa + \kappa^!$. | Load-bearing numerical constants must be derived in-place from defining axioms: Virasoro OPE $T(z)T(w) = \tfrac{c/2}{(z-w)^4} + \tfrac{2T(w)}{(z-w)^2} + \tfrac{\partial T(w)}{z-w}$, or mode relations $[L_m, L_n] = (m-n)L_{m+n} + \tfrac{c}{12}(m^3-m)\delta_{m+n,0}$. State normalization conventions explicitly. Cross-check by $\ge 3$ independent paths (mode expansion, OPE contraction, Kac determinant / singular-vector). Citation is a sanity check after the derivation, not a substitute. | citation-as-derivation substitution (load-bearing constants) |
| 275 | "Topologization is proved for affine Kac-Moody at non-critical level." (Or analogously: "Theorem holds away from critical / admissible / resonant level" without obstruction statement.) | There is a genuine proof valid for $k \ne -h^\vee$; the critical-level obstruction is real and has well-known mathematical content. | Stating "proved at non-critical level" without identifying the critical-level obstruction treats $k = -h^\vee$ as a technicality. At critical level the centre of the affine VOA becomes infinite-dimensional (Feigin-Frenkel: $Z(V_{-h^\vee}(\mathfrak{g})) \cong \mathrm{Fun}(\mathrm{Op}_{{}^L\mathfrak{g}}(D^\times))$), the Sugawara conformal vector is undefined, and the argument using $\omega$ cannot even be stated — the obstruction is not a bug, it is the content. | Every "proved at non-critical level" (or analogous scope-qualifier) claim must be accompanied by (a) a remark stating what fails at the excluded level with mathematical content (centre becomes Op-algebra, Sugawara undefined, normalization denominator vanishes, etc.), (b) whether the conjecture admits a repaired statement at the excluded level via a named duality (Feigin-Frenkel, Wakimoto resolution, geometric Langlands dictionary), (c) whether the obstruction is local (isolated bad levels) or global (entire families). | scope-qualifier without obstruction statement |
| 276 | Bare "$E_n$-chiral algebra" (typically $E_1$- or $E_2$-chiral) without specifying which of the $\ge 5$ distinct notions is meant. | Each of the notions is a real object with its own natural derived centre; the programme needs all of them at different points. | At least five non-equivalent notions coexist: (A) $A_\infty$-algebra in factorizable $D$-modules on $X$; (B) operad map $A_\infty \to \mathrm{End}^{\mathrm{ch}}_A$ with meromorphic structure maps; (C) operad map $E_2^{\mathrm{homot}} \to \mathrm{End}^{\mathrm{ch}}_A$; (D) $A_\infty$-algebra in the category of $E_1$-chiral algebras (inner chiral + outer algebraic); (E) iterated $A_\infty$-in-$A_\infty$-in-factorizable-$D$-modules. No equivalence is established among them, and each has its own derived centre on its own operad. | Before writing any statement about "$E_n$-chiral algebra" or "derived centre of an $E_n$-chiral algebra": name the notion (A/B/C/D/E or a sixth), name the matching centre construction, name the output operad, and — if claiming $E_3$ — state the conformal-vector / non-critical-level hypothesis. Inscribe a definition block once per chapter fixing the notion, cross-reference the standalone memory register of notions. | E_n-chiral notion unspecified |
| 277 | "$\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is an $E_3$-operad" (or is invoked as an $E_3$-structure on $A$). | Swiss-cheese $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is the correct intermediary between $E_1$-chiral and $E_3$; the $E_3$ promotion exists in appropriate cases. | $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ is bicoloured (two object classes: meromorphic-holomorphic disks and topological balls) with asymmetric mixed operations (no closed-to-open action); Dunn additivity $E_2 \otimes E_1 = E_3$ applies to single-colour operads and therefore does NOT identify $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ with $E_3$ on the nose. Promotion to $E_3$ requires an additional hypothesis (a conformal vector / Sugawara construction at non-critical level) that implements the topologization of the holomorphic direction. | State $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ explicitly as the bicoloured intermediary operad. Compare AP167 (topologization PROVED for affine KM at non-critical level; CONJECTURAL for general). | SC bicoloured vs E_3 single-coloured conflation |
| 278 | "Holographic" applied to a statement (e.g. "boundary-linear bulk", "$E_n$-$E_{n-1}$ holographic duality") without naming the specific bulk-boundary identification at chain level. | The programme's holographic picture $H(T) = (A, A^!, C, r(z), \Theta_A, \nabla^{\mathrm{hol}})$ is a real structure with four recovery theorems, and holography is a genuine organizing principle. | "Holographic" as narrative replaces the named chain-level map with a metaphor. The actual content is: a bulk object (Hochschild cochains / derived centre / $E_n$) recovers a boundary object (algebra / $E_{n-1}$) via an explicit pullback along a specified inclusion of operads, with specified homotopy data (r-matrix, MC element, flat connection). Without the explicit map, "holographic" is rhetorical. | Every "holographic" / "bulk-boundary" / "open-closed" claim must name: (i) which object is bulk, which is boundary, (ii) the specific operadic inclusion $\mathcal{O}_{\partial} \hookrightarrow \mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{bulk}}$ or the specific restriction map $Z^{\mathrm{der}}(A) \to A$, (iii) the homotopy data (r-matrix, MC, connection) that witnesses the relation, (iv) the scope (Koszul locus? Global? Proved at formal disk but conjectural at finite-radius disk?). The global boundary-linear-bulk triangle is CONJECTURAL beyond the Koszul locus. | holography as narrative without operadic map |
| 296 | "Topological Hochschild" is used for the classical cochain complex $\RHom_{A^e}(A,A)$ or for bare $\HH^\bullet(A)$ of a discrete algebra. | There is a real comparison between classical algebraic Hochschild cochains and the spectrum-level circle trace. | Conflates two different outputs and two different ambient categories: classical algebraic Hochschild cochains $\HH^\bullet_{\mathrm{alg}}(A)=\RHom_{A^e}(A,A)$ live in chain complexes over a point, while $\THH(R)=R \otimes^{\mathbf L}_{R \otimes R^{\mathrm{op}}} R$ lives in spectra with an $S^1$-action. | 297 | Theorem~H or a degree-$\{0,1,2\}$ concentration claim is advertised as a theorem about bare "Hochschild" without naming the chiral theory. | There is a genuine concentration theorem in the programme. | The proof of Theorem~H is curve-specific: it uses chiral OPE residues, ordered/symmetric Fulton--MacPherson configuration spaces, PBW/Koszul collapse of the chiral bar complex, and the curve-level Verdier shift. | 279 | A proposition labeled `ClaimStatusProvedHere` as a PTVV/derived-stack bypass of Theorem C is independent of Theorem C. | Every inscribed proof labeled `ProvedHere` is genuinely self-contained and does not import the theorem whose bypass it claims. | `prop:ptvv-lagrangian` imports the Verdier pairing (output of Theorem C) at `higher_genus_complementarity.tex:2219-2222` and `thm:quantum-complementarity-main` at `:2240-2245`; the "independent bypass" is therefore conditional on Theorem C, not independent. | Any proposition framed as "independent of / bypass of / alternative to $X$" must have a proof body that does not invoke $X$, any corollary of $X$, or any object constructed via $X$. | 284 | "There are $N$ equivalent characterisations of chiral Koszulness" (or similar: "$N$ equivalent notions of integrability", "$N$ versions of conformality") stated as a headline fact without a star-shaped or cyclic implication diagram inscribed. | The programme does collect $N$ distinct chiral-Koszulness characterisations on some class, and Ginzburg-Kapranov-style bar-cobar + operadic Koszul theorems do provide genuine equivalences. | "$N$ equivalent" asserts pairwise equivalence — $N(N-1)/2$ implications — but most manuscripts prove at most a spanning tree ($N-1$ implications) or a cycle ($N$ implications). Without the inscribed implication structure, any missing implication becomes a silent gap. In particular "D-module purity" added as the 13th characterisation requires two directions (purity $\Rightarrow$ Koszul; Koszul $\Rightarrow$ purity) each of which has its own proof content and its own scope. | Every "$N$ equivalent characterisations" statement must be accompanied by an inscribed implication diagram (star-shaped with a distinguished canonical definition at the centre, or cyclic with a named cycle order). Each implication arrow must have a named proof anchor (lemma / proposition / theorem with \label). Additional characterisations (e.g., D-module purity as the 13th) require both directions proved separately, each with its own scope and hypothesis. | equivalence claim without inscribed implication structure |
| 285 | "$U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X$ is the universal factorization envelope" (or analogous: "the universal envelope", "the universal construction", "the canonical chiral algebra"). | There is a genuine construction $U^{\mathrm{mod}}_X$ built from a Lie-algebra input by a chiral-BD universal-enveloping procedure, and it has a real role in averaging and MC. | "Universal" without a universal property is narrative. A universal construction must be (i) a functor $F: \mathcal{C} \to \mathcal{D}$, (ii) left adjoint to a named forgetful $G: \mathcal{D} \to \mathcal{C}$ (or right, or initial/terminal in a specific comma category), (iii) with the adjunction unit $\eta: 1 \to GF$ inscribed. Without all three, "universal" is a label, not a theorem — and subsequent arguments that invoke universality (e.g., "by universality, the map factors uniquely") are unanchored. | Every "universal" claim must be paired with the universal property: state the source and target categories with explicit morphism classes; state the functor's left/right adjoint partner; prove the adjunction (or the initial/terminal property) with the unit/counit inscribed. If the universal property cannot be proved, downgrade "universal envelope" to "canonical construction" or "specific construction" — and audit downstream arguments that relied on universality. | universal without universal property |
| 286 | $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}}$ (Swiss-cheese bicoloured operad) treated as self-dual — implicitly or explicitly — under Koszul duality of operads; or $\mathsf{SC}^! \simeq \mathsf{SC}$ asserted or assumed. | Self-duality holds (up to shift) for single-colour $E_n$ operads, and $\mathsf{SC}$'s Koszul dual does exist as a bicoloured object. | For bicoloured operads $\mathsf{SC}(E_1, E_2)$, Koszul duality flips each colour separately to its Koszul dual ($E_1 \mapsto \mathrm{Lie}$, $E_2 \mapsto E_2[1]$) AND dualizes the mixed open-closed operations (shuffle-mixed in the dual). Result: $\mathsf{SC}^! = (\mathrm{Lie}, \mathrm{Ass}, \mathrm{shuffle\text{-}mixed})$ (AP166). The asymmetry of the mixed operations means $\mathsf{SC}$ is NOT self-dual even up to shift. | State $\mathsf{SC}^{\mathrm{ch,top}} \ne \mathsf{SC}^!$ explicitly in any context invoking Koszul duality of the Swiss-cheese operad. Koszul-dualize each colour separately and verify the mixed-operation dualization; the shuffle-mixed part is the distinguishing feature. Any proof step using "by self-duality of Swiss-cheese" is WRONG — inscribe the correct bicoloured dual and re-run the proof. | bicoloured operad treated as self-dual |
| 287 | "The Drinfeld double $D^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)$ of the chiral algebra $A$ ..." | 288 | Bare $r(z)$ (classical / chiral $r$-matrix) appearing in a formula without level / central-charge / family prefix. | Each witness family has a specific, derivable $r(z)$ with its own level scaling: $r^{\mathrm{Heis}}(z) = k/z$, $r^{KM}(z) = k\Omega/z$, $r^{\mathrm{Vir}}(z) = (c/2)/z^3 + 2T/z$. | A bare $r(z)$ elides the level scaling. | 293 | The Arnold relation $\eta_{ij}\wedge\eta_{jk}+\eta_{jk}\wedge\eta_{ki}+\eta_{ki}\wedge\eta_{ij}=0$ is the unique defining relation for $H^*(\operatorname{Conf}_n(X))$ on every smooth curve $X$. | The genus-$0$ local propagator relation is real and does control the affine ordered bar differential. | Conflates the genus-$0$ tangent-screen identity with the global cohomology of configuration spaces on $\mathbb{P}^1$ and on $\Sigma_g$, $g\ge1$. On $\mathbb{P}^1$, $\mathrm{PSL}_2$ gauge fixing imposes linear relations $\sum_{j\neq i}\bar\eta_{ij}=0$; on $\Sigma_g$, point-pushing couples puncture classes to ambient $H^1(\Sigma_g)$, so the $\eta_{ij}$ are not closed classes by themselves. | Arnold is complete only on $\mathbb{A}^1$ / formal-disk screens. | 307 | One symbol $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)$ stands for both the Hodge supertrace $\sum_{q=0}^{d}(-1)^{q}h^{0,q}(X)=\chi(\cO_X)$ and the operational K\"unneth-additive chiral modular characteristic of the quantum chiral algebra $\Phi_d(D^b\Coh(X))$, and the identity $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(X)=\chi(\cO_X)$ is claimed globally on compact CY$_d$. | On the proved CY$_2$ slice with $h^{1,0}(X)=0$, the Serre-duality parity argument does kill the one-loop correction and the two invariants coincide at $\chi(\cO_X)$; the Hodge supertrace is genuinely what Serre-theoretic machinery computes; the K\"unneth-additive characteristic is what the product route and Mukai-rank computations produce; each is a real Vol~III invariant with its own compute-layer verification. | Two invariants are collapsed into one symbol. Concrete counterexample: on $K3\times E$ in complex dimension $3$, $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}(K3\times E)=\chi(\cO_{K3})\cdot\chi(\cO_E)=2\cdot 0=0$ while $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(K3\times E)=\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(K3)+\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}(E)=2+1=3$. The three strata are disjoint and the bare-$\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ / Hodge-supertrace coincidence is proved only on the CY$_2$ slice with $h^{1,0}=0$. | Every Vol~III $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ appearance must disambiguate: write $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}^{\mathrm{Hodge}}(X)$ for the Serre supertrace $\sum_q(-1)^q h^{0,q}$, and keep bare $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ exclusively for the K\"unneth-additive operational chiral modular characteristic produced by $\Phi_d(D^b\Coh(X))$. | 318 | Reader-facing manuscript prose pontificates about previous incorrect versions or historical author-errors: ``The naive six-way isomorphism of the original CY-C is therefore falsified'', ``The earlier hypothesis $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ was refuted at $K = 3$'', ``the earlier $\fgl(4 \mid 20)$ designation is a misnomer'', ``previously it was conjectured that...'', ``in an earlier formulation...'', ``X is refuted by the data, unlike the original claim of...''. | Falsifying a naive ansatz, a competing definition, or a plausible-looking guess is a real mathematical act — and standalone-rigorous exposition must compare against the naive guess to motivate the correct definition. Beilinson's dictum (``what limits forward progress is the inability to dismiss false ideas'') is a correct epistemic discipline. | The error is orienting the comparison along the author's own historical timeline rather than along mathematical naivety. A reader of a standalone monograph has no access to (and no interest in) the manuscript's prior drafts, earlier conjectures, or retractions; naming them as ``the original X'', ``the earlier Y'', ``formerly claimed Z'' imports the author's memoir into the reader's space. It reads as apologetic signposting rather than mathematics, and it dates the manuscript: a reader three years later has no referent for ``the original CY-C''. The same falsification content can be expressed as a mathematical comparison with a NAIVE GUESS (a reader-level candidate, not an author-timeline candidate); this is stronger because the naive-guess comparison is timeless, reader-facing, and substantiates the correct definition. The prose template ``Naively one might expect X; Y obstructs this; instead, Z holds'' is the reader-facing form; ``the original W was wrong; we now know V'' is the author-facing form. | Manuscript prose replaces every historical-author-timeline phrasing with a naive-candidate comparison: \emph{instead of} ``The earlier hypothesis $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ was refuted at $K = 3$'', \emph{write} ``A naive exponential ansatz $D_K = 18^{K-1}$ would predict $D_3 = 324$; the direct value $D_3 = 972$ rules it out, and the sequence is governed instead by~\ldots''. \emph{Instead of} ``the earlier $\fgl(4 \mid 20)$ designation is a misnomer'', \emph{write} the correct label with a sentence on why the alternative fails on the form-structure. \emph{Instead of} ``The naive six-way isomorphism of the original CY-C is falsified'', \emph{write} ``Naively one might expect all six routes to assemble into a single Hopf object; the generator-rank stratification $\rho^{R_i} \in \{3, 12, 24\}$ obstructs the common quotient''. Sweep signatures in preface / abstract / introduction / chapter-lead prose: ``the original'', ``was refuted'', ``was falsified'', ``the earlier'', ``earlier hypothesis'', ``previously'', ``formerly'', ``in an earlier formulation'', ``in a prior version''. Each instance gets rewritten as a naive-candidate comparison or deleted. The manuscript is a standalone mathematical object, not a commentary on its own history. Related: AP186 (shallow correction vs substantive heal), AP312 (author-discipline jargon leakage). | AI-slop: reader-facing prose pontificates about past author errors / retracted claims / earlier versions |

The E-direction supplies the bi-based Ran-factorisation parameter (spectral) rather than grading. At separating-node factorisation 1/Phi_{10} -> 1/eta^{24}(tau) * 1/phi_{10,1}(rho) the single eta^{24} factor confirms one copy of the Mukai rank, not two. | W15-Tannakian-neutrality-scope | Rep(H_Delta5) is (or is not) neutral Tannakian globally on A_2-bar. | Rep(H_Delta5) is Tannakian in some appropriate sense; Deligne 1990 reconstruction applies. | Globally on A_2-bar the 3-cocycle associator tilde-Phi^{Sieg-Bor}[Phi_{10}/eta^{24}] defines a nontrivial mu_8 gerbe on H_1 u H_4; on the open complement the gerbe is trivialisable. | W16-c2d-prime-107-factorisation | c_{2d}(A_1, Sigma_{0,24}, all max) = -312 = -24 * 13 with 13 = c_{4d}/2 interpretable as the bosonic-string critical dimension and 24 = chi(K3). | The Beem-Rastelli factor c_{2d} = -12 c_{4d} is correct; the class-S evaluation on Sigma_{0,24} is a well-defined number. | The Wave-14 ansatz c_{4d}(A_1, Sigma_{g,n}) = (12(g-1) + 7n)/6 giving c_{4d} = 26 at (0,24) fails the SU(2) N_f = 4 cross-check: at (0,4) it returns 8/3 whereas Shapere-Tachikawa 2008 Tab 4 and Tachikawa 2013 eq (13.6) give 7/6. Hence -312 = -24*13 is not the correct first-principles value. | Canonical first-principles value: c_{4d}(A_1, Sigma_{0,n}, all max) = (5n - 13)/6 (Shapere-Tachikawa 2008 Sec 3; Chacaltana-Distler 2010 eq (5.14)), giving at n = 24: c_{4d} = 107/6 and c_{2d} = -12 * 107/6 = -2 * 107 = -214. The integer 107 is PRIME, so -214 admits no non-trivial integer factorisation apart from -2 * 107. The earlier "-24 * 13 = -312" numerology is a false-because-wrong-ansatz cache trap. Shadow tower at c = -214: S_2 = -107, S_3 = 2, S_4 = 5/112136, S_5 = 3/3000319; Zamolodchikov norm = 22427.2 > 0 (class M, generic stratum). Mock-modular weight assignment: NOT -c/24 = 107/12 (non-integer), but Siegel weight 5 via Gritsenko-Nikulin Delta_5 = sqrt(Phi_10). c_{eff} = c - 24 h_{min} = -214 + 48 = -166 = -2 * 83. Class-M heptagon face robust under -312 -> -214 retraction: both values in generic class-M stratum (nonvanishing 5c+22, S_4, Q_c irreducible). | W16-siegel-weight-5-vs-elliptic-integer | Mock-modular weight at K3 base point equals -c_{2d}/24 = 107/12. | Chiral partition function is a mock-modular form on some modular group. | 107/12 is NOT an integer, so the naive Cardy-regime weight -c/24 reading as an elliptic modular weight on SL_2(Z) fails type-check. | Correct modular covariance is SIEGEL (on Sp_4(Z)) not elliptic: partition function is a Siegel modular form of weight 5 on the Gritsenko-Nikulin double cover of Sp_4(Z), identified with Delta_5 = Phi_{10}^{1/2}. Weight 5 is determined by Borcherds denominator degree 10 and square-root refinement, INDEPENDENT of c_{2d}. The bridge elliptic <-> Siegel is the Humbert-H_1 restriction, under which Delta_5 descends to a weight-5 Jacobi form of elliptic index 1 (NOT a weight-107/12 scalar modular form). | W17-BKM-Gram-principal-minor-vs-eigenvalues | Signature of the rank-3 Feingold-Frenkel hyperbolic Gram matrix G_BKM (entries {2,-2,-2}, symmetric) can be read off Sylvester's principal minors. | The rank-3 Gram is real symmetric, so its signature is a well-defined invariant; principal-minor tests DO work for strictly positive-definite matrices (leading minors all > 0 iff positive-definite). | The principal-minor ladder for G_BKM is (2, 0, -32): the 2x2 leading minor vanishes because alpha_1 + alpha_2 is isotropic in the {alpha_1, alpha_2}-subspace. Sylvester's criterion requires non-degenerate leading minors; when the 2x2 minor is exactly 0, Sylvester is silent and reading the signature from the ladder is invalid. A hasty Sylvester read would give (+, 0, -) which conflates with signature (1, 1, 1) or (2, 1, 0) -- the wrong answer is "hyperbolic with one null direction" rather than "hyperbolic (2,1) with isotropic 2-plane combination". | Compute eigenvalues directly: char poly = -lambda^3 + 6 lambda^2 - 32 has real roots {+4, +4, -2}, so signature is (2, 1). The isotropic combination alpha_1 + alpha_2 (giving m_2 = 0) is an artifact of the S_3-symmetric Cartan structure, NOT a null direction in the ambient (2,1)-Lorentzian form. Cross-verify via Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 Thm 1.1: BKM g_{Delta_5} has real-root lattice II_{2,1} by construction (paramodular weight 5 via singular-theta lift on O(2,1) Grassmannian), so signature (2,1) is FORCED by the Borcherds lift independent of the eigenvalue computation. Primary: Feingold-Frenkel 1983 Math Ann 263 Thm 1.1; Gritsenko-Nikulin 1998 AJM 120 Thm 1.1; Kac 1990 Infinite Dim Lie Algebras Ch 14. | principal-minor-vs-eigenvalue-signature |
| W17-positive-energy-unitarity-vs-ambient-indefiniteness | "Unitary module of H_Delta5" means positive-definite inner product on the whole BKM representation. | Unitarity is a real, well-defined invariant for highest-weight modules over Kac-Moody and BKM algebras; there exist unitary highest-weight modules in this setting. | For a BKM algebra with hyperbolic Cartan, the BKM inner product is INDEFINITE Hermitian: signature (infty real-root positive, infty imaginary-root negative). No finite positive-definite projection captures the full BKM content; "unitary module" as a global Hilbert-space statement is impossible. | Unitarity statements must specify: (a) SUBMODULE SCOPE (real-root sector, positive-definite 2-plane P subset Cartan of signature (2,1) per W17-BKM-Gram) and (b) WEIGHT CONSTRAINT (lambda in P^*_+ AND (lambda, lambda) > 0; spacelike condition). Positive-energy unitary representations are {V^lambda : lambda in P^*_+, (lambda, lambda) > 0}, constructed as Frenkel-Kac vertex algebras on the positive-definite rank-2 lattice. Imaginary-root representations (timelike (lambda, lambda) < 0) are NOT unitary -- negative-norm ground state. The Fricke-fixed sub-MTC is Z/2-graded, fixed points projectively self-dual. | W17-Niemeier-breakdown-at-N6 | The umbral moonshine labelling $X_N = (24/N) A_{N-1}$ extends the Mathieu-moonshine $24 A_1$ observation to all $N \ge 2$ indefinitely. | Cheng-Duncan-Harvey 2014 Tab 1 gives a finite list of 23 Niemeier lattices each attached to an umbral group; every Niemeier lattice has root-system rank 24. | At $N = 6$, the hypothetical root system $4 A_5$ is NOT among the 23 Niemeier root systems (Niemeier 1973 list; Conway-Sloane 1988 Ch 16). | W17-c-eff-negative-as-anomaly-not-entanglement | At c_eff = -166, the Calabrese-Cardy entropy S_EE = (c_eff/3) log(L/eps) = -(166/3) log(L/eps) is a bona fide negative entanglement entropy of H_Delta5. | Calabrese-Cardy entanglement law is universal for 2d CFTs with central charge c; c_eff replaces c in non-unitary / negative-c_{2d} situations for partition functions (Cardy counting per W16-c2d). | Entanglement entropy S = -tr(rho log rho) is non-negative by construction; a negative coefficient c_eff/3 < 0 cannot be a physical entanglement entropy on a Hilbert space. Conflates "partition-function coefficient" (which CAN be negative for non-unitary CFTs) with "entanglement entropy of a Hilbert-space density matrix" (which CANNOT). | Separate the two readings: (i) c_eff/3 log(L/eps) is the GRAVITATIONAL/TOPOLOGICAL ANOMALY coefficient governing the holographic dual's topological entanglement (Manschot-Moore 2007; DVV 1997 anti-holomorphic counting); (ii) the genuine unitary entanglement comes from the real-root submodule V^unit with rank-2 lattice central charge c_unit = rk(P) = 2, giving positive Calabrese-Cardy S = (2/3) log(L/eps) > 0. The negative c_eff = -166 quantifies HOW FAR H_Delta5 is from a unitary CFT, not an entropy. On Humbert divisors H_1 and H_4 (off the Koszul locus), the hyperbolic Cartan degenerates to full-rank-collapse, unitarity breaks on real-root sector too, and logarithmic-CFT corrections c_log log^2(L/eps) appear. | W18-wall-of-walls-commutator-obstruction-vs-Malcev-cocycle | The non-vanishing commutator class [gamma_i, gamma_j] in H^2_et(H_i cap H_j, Z/N_{ij}) at the codimension-2 wall-of-walls of the Humbert stratum in Abar_2 is an obstruction to strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion of H_Delta5; consequently strict chain-level inversion is impossible at the wall-of-walls. | The commutator class is real, nonzero, and computed via Bruinier cup Kuga-Satake / Bruinier cup pentagon / pentagon cup Kuga-Satake; it genuinely obstructs the pro-object Mayer-Vietoris gluing in the single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient of Definition monodromy-refined-total-bar-weight. | Treating the commutator class as an absolute obstruction conflates two ambients: (i) the single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient (where the class is an obstruction); (ii) the Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient (where the class is the classifying cocycle of the Malcev extension of the bi-unipotent structure, and the Schmid-Cattani-Kaplan commuting-sl_2-triples canonically split it). An obstruction-in-ambient-X is not an obstruction-in-ambient-Y when Y strictly refines X. Pattern-236 / Pattern-269 scope discipline. | The commutator class is the classifying cocycle of a Malcev extension; strict chain-level inversion holds in the Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient (Definition def:deligne-malcev-bi-unipotent-ambient of chapter mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex) via the curvature-corrected bi-graded Bott-Koszul chain homotopy h^{(chi_i,chi_j,k_i,k_j)}_{H_i cap H_j} = M^{(chi_i,chi_j)} (N_i + N_j + lambda_{k_i,k_j})^{-1} (id + sigma h^{(g)})^{-1} sigma (eq:wall-of-walls-chain-homotopy). The chain-homotopy identity [d^{Gamma tensor Gamma}, h^{Gamma tensor Gamma}] = id - p^{Gamma tensor Gamma} (eq:wall-of-walls-chain-homotopy-identity) holds, and Mittag-Leffler on the bi-graded tower follows from finite-dimensionality of gr^{k_i, k_j}_W F^{<=w, chi_i, chi_j}. The pentachotomy of Corollary cor:sharpened-quadrichotomy-after-monodromy-refinement is upgraded to a hexachotomy, and global strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion holds on the full Humbert stratum H_1 cup H_3 cup H_4 in the (single-refined / bi-refined) pro-ambient cover. | W19-phi-n-four-conflicting-objects | Bare $\phi^{(n)}$ is used for all of: (i) the Drinfeld associator coefficient, (ii) the KZ period on $M_{0,4}$, (iii) a shadow-tower entry $S_r$, (iv) the Etingof-Kazhdan pentagon coboundary of nilpotent_completion.tex. | Each of the four notions is a real construction and appears at distinct points in the programme; naming them uniformly "$\phi^{(n)}$" is a local convenience. | The four objects are genuinely different: (i) lives in the group-like completion of the free Lie algebra on two generators with MZV coefficients; (ii) is a scalar function on $M_{0,4}$ given by iterated integration; (iii) is a rational function of the chiral central charge $c$ (Virasoro) or level $k$ (affine KM); (iv) is the Maurer-Cartan obstruction at $\hbar^n$ in the super-Drinfeld associator expansion, normalised by $n!$. They have different ambient categories, different normalisations, different scopes, and different growth rates. Using the bare label "$\phi^{(n)}$" for all four invites AP113/AP152/AP160-style bare-label confusions: statements proved for one notion silently transport to another where they fail. | The programme's canonical $\phi^{(n)}$ is notion (iv), the Etingof-Kazhdan pentagon coboundary, as fixed by Definition def:phi-n-pent-EK in chapters/theory/shadow_tower_higher_coefficients.tex. The MZV leg is $(1/n!)\sum_{i=1}^{d_n} c_n^{(i)}\,\mathrm{MZV}_i^{(n)}$ in the Brown-Deligne canonical basis, with $c_n^{(i)} = 1$ from the Drinfeld-Deligne duality (Brown 2012 Thm 4.1). The Borcherds leg $(1/n!)\Phi_{10}^{n/2}\eta^{-12n} c_n^{(K3)}$ is K3-lattice-specific, with $c_n^{(K3)}$ Hardy-Ramanujan-bounded. For $n \le 12$ the MZV leg is unconditional (Brown 2011 Thm 1.1, Thm 1.2); for $n = 13$ it is unconditional through depth 3 and Broadhurst-Kreimer-trivial above; for $n \ge 14$ it is conditional on the Zagier-Hoffman depth-reduction conjecture (Brown 2012 arXiv:1301.3053 Conj. 2). Every bare "$\phi^{(n)}$" must name the notion from (i)-(iv) and its ambient. | W18-ambient-refinement-principle-chain-level-bar-cobar | "Strict chain-level bar-cobar inversion fails on locus L" is an ambient-independent statement. | A strict chain-level quasi-isomorphism is a well-defined notion in Ch(Vect), in pro-Ch(Vect), and in every refinement thereof; each ambient produces a well-defined yes/no for inversion on a given locus L. | "Fails on L" is actually ambient-dependent. Strict chain-level inversion can fail in a coarser pro-ambient and hold in a finer pro-ambient that retains more of the geometric data (conformal weight filtration, monodromy filtration, bi-monodromy bi-filtration). The locus L together with the ambient is what carries the yes/no datum. Writing "fails on L" without the ambient qualifier is Pattern-236 scope conflation. | Every chain-level bar-cobar inversion statement is ambient-qualified. The hexachotomy of Remark rem:wall-of-walls-obstruction-as-extension-class of chapter mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex gives six ambient readings for H_Delta5 on Abar_2: (1) fibrewise on generic points of U; (2) single-monodromy-refined pro-ambient on O_hat^circ_{H_1 cup H_3 cup H_4}; (3) Deligne-Malcev bi-unipotent pro-ambient on the wall-of-walls O_hat_{H_i cap H_j}; (4) weight-completed coderived on Abar_2; (5) A_infty-corrected on a neighbourhood of H_3; (6) (infty,1)-categorical in Perf(Abar_2) via Deligne nearby cycles. Each reads the bar-cobar counit as a strict / weight-completed / A_infty-corrected / (infty,1)-categorical quasi-isomorphism in its respective ambient; the six ambients form a partial order of refinements, and statements transport upward. Primary: Positselski 2011 Mem AMS 212; Schmid 1973; Cattani-Kaplan-Schmid 1986; Vol I chapters/theory/mc5_class_m_chain_level_platonic.tex Corollary cor:global-strict-bar-cobar-humbert-stratum. | chain-level-ambient-refinement |
| W19-LDP-variance-inverse-density-vs-curvature | The Gaussian variance $\sigma_k^2$ in the local LDP rate $I_k(\theta^*_k + \delta) = \delta^2/(2\sigma_k^2) + O(\delta^3)$ for Fricke-phase clustering at node $\theta^*_k = k\pi/8$ coincides with the density curvature $|\rho''(\theta^*_k)|^{-1}$, giving $\sigma_k^2 = (\pi^2/2)\cos^{-2}(\theta^*_k)$. | The density-curvature coefficient $\cos(2\theta^*_k)$ and the LDP Cramér variance are both genuine quantities attached to the Sato--Tate density $\rho(\theta) = (2/\pi)\sin^2\theta$ at a fixed angle. | Density-curvature (second Taylor coefficient of $\rho$) governs the behaviour of the density itself; the LDP variance governs the entropy cost of a fluctuation. They are related but not equal. The Gärtner--Ellis quadratic LDP at an interior point where $\rho > 0$ yields $\sigma_k^2 = \rho(\theta^*_k)^{-1}$ (inverse density, Bayes-type), not $|\rho''|^{-1}$; the proposed $\cos^{-2}$ formula diverges at $k = 2, 6$ where $\cos(2\theta^*_k) = 0$ even though the density is finite and positive there, proving the formula wrong. | At interior nodes $k \in \{1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7\}$ the correct Gaussian LDP curvature is $\sigma_k^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(\theta^*_k))$ (three-path verified via: Cramér-transform Legendre, Sanov relative-entropy Taylor expansion, empirical-histogram Bayes/inverse-density). Values: $\sigma_1^2 = \sigma_7^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(\pi/8)) \approx 10.73$; $\sigma_2^2 = \sigma_6^2 = \pi$; $\sigma_3^2 = \sigma_5^2 = \pi/(2\sin^2(3\pi/8)) \approx 1.84$; $\sigma_4^2 = \pi/2 \approx 1.57$. At boundary nodes $k \in \{0, 8\}$ where $\rho = 0$, the Gaussian expansion degenerates and the LDP shifts to Poisson regime with $I^{\mathrm{Poi}}_0(t) = t\log(t/\mu_0) - t + \mu_0$, $\mu_0(\delta) = (2/(3\pi))\delta^3$. Scope: unconditional for $\Delta_{E_6} = f_{16}$ (non-CM cuspidal GL_2/Q eigenform) via Newton--Thorne 2021 Thm A establishing Sym$^n$ automorphy for all $n \ge 1$, removing the Barnet-Lamb--Geraghty--Harris--Taylor 2011 conditional hypothesis. Primary: Dembo--Zeitouni 2010 \emph{Large Deviations Techniques} 2e Thm 2.1.4, Thm 4.2.1, Thm 6.2.10, §3.7; Barnet-Lamb--Geraghty--Harris--Taylor 2011 Publ IHÉS 108 Thm B (effective Sato--Tate, conditional on Sym$^n$); Newton--Thorne 2021 Publ IHÉS 134 Thm A (unconditional Sym$^n$); Taylor 2008 Publ IHÉS 108 (Sato--Tate for modular forms); Lamzouri 2019 J Reine Angew Math 744 (L-function moment asymptotics). | W19-mu16-banding-metaplectic-H4 | The $\mu_8$-gerbe banding $F_{ij} = [\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]^{1/8}$-ratio of Theorem thm:modtr-wave18-banding-cocycle on $U = \overline{\mathcal A_2}\setminus(H_1\cup H_4)$ is the maximal chain-level banding; naive extension to $\overline{\mathcal A_2}\setminus H_1$ lands in $\mu_8$. | The $\mu_8$-cocycle exists on $U$ and satisfies the \v Cech closure. The $H^2$-class on the full Humbert divisor has the decomposition $\mu_8\cdot[H_1] + \mu_{16}\cdot[H_4]$ (Bruinier 2002 Prop. 5.1). | The $H_4$ obstruction has order 16, not 8, because (i) $\mathrm{ord}_{H_4}(\Phi_{10}) = 2$ gives $\Phi_{10}^{1/8}$ monodromy $\zeta_4$ of order 4, but on the metaplectic double cover (forced by Kuga-Satake period doubling, Morrison 1984 Thm 3) the combined monodromy has order $\mathrm{lcm}(8,16) = 16$. The $\mu_8$-cocycle cannot extend across $H_4$: the Fricke-involution $w_8$ eigenvalue on $\Delta_5^{1/8}$ is $\zeta_{16}$, order 16. | Pass to Mp cover: $G_{ij} := [\Delta_5/\eta^{12}]^{1/8}|_{\widetilde U_i}/[\Delta_5/\eta^{12}]^{1/8}|_{\widetilde U_j} \in \mu_{16}$ is the refined cocycle on $\widetilde V = \pi_{\mathrm{Mp}}^{-1}(\overline{\mathcal A_2}\setminus H_1)$, with $G_{ij}|_U^2 = F_{ij}$ (since $\widetilde s_i^2 = s_i$). Three verification paths: (V1) \v Cech $\delta G = 0$ telescoping; (V2) Bockstein $\beta\colon H^2(V,\mu_{16})\to H^3(V,\mathbb Z)$ cross-check gives $\langle \beta[G_V],\gamma_{H_4}\rangle = 3/16$, generating $\mathbb Z/16$; (V3) Fricke $w_8$ eigenvalue on $\widetilde{\mathcal G}|_{H_4}$ is $\zeta_{16}+\zeta_{16}^{-1} = 2\cos(\pi/8)$. The $\mu_{16}$-refinement is orthogonal to the two-$\hbar$ AP151 bridge: $\hbar_{\mathrm{qg}}^2 = -1/8$ is invariant under $\zeta^{16}\to\zeta^8$ sheet-descent. | W18-enriques-bkm-M12-direct-moonshine-fails | The Enriques elliptic genus $\phi^{\mathrm{En}}_{0,1}$ decomposes as $\sum \dim V_n^{M_{12}} \cdot (\text{virtual } M_{12}\text{-module})$, giving a direct $M_{24}$-style moonshine for $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Enr}}$ with Mathieu group $M_{12}$ acting on virtual mock-modular multiplicities. | The Enriques elliptic genus is the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold $\phi^{\mathrm{En}}_{0,1} = \tfrac{1}{2}\phi^{\mathrm{K3}}_{0,1}$ (Borisov--Libgober 1998 Thm 4.2); sporadic-symmetry acting on its Fourier coefficients is a real phenomenon, and $M_{12}\subset M_{24}$ is a genuine maximal subgroup (point stabiliser). | Leading coefficient $f_{\mathrm{En}}(0,1)=10$ is NOT an irreducible $M_{12}$-dimension (ATLAS p.32 irrep dimensions $\{1,11,11,16,16,45,54,55,55,55,66,99,120,144,176\}$). The direct $M_{24}$-template fails at the first Fourier coefficient. Stating "$M_{12}$-moonshine for Enriques" without the orbifold intermediary is a template-mismatch conflation. | The correct moonshine for $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}^{\mathrm{Enr}}$ is \emph{second-quantised / generalised} Mathieu moonshine \`a la Persson--Volpato 2013 (arXiv:1312.0622): the $M_{12}$ action arises as point-stabiliser in $M_{24}$ on the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold sector, with Fourier coefficients of $\phi^{\mathrm{En}}_{0,1}$ decomposing as \emph{half-sums} of $M_{24}$ virtual characters restricted along $M_{12}\hookrightarrow M_{24}$. Paramodular level $K(2)$, Siegel weight $5/2$ on $\widetilde{\mathrm{Sp}_4}$, Lambda_{\mathrm{Enr}}=E_8(-1)\oplus\mathrm{II}_{1,1}$ signature $(1,9)$. | W19-chenevier-pseudocharacter-source-algebra | A $4$-dimensional pseudo-character $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ "for $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$" (the chiral bialgebra) encodes the trace data of the Galois representation $\phi_{\Delta_{10}}\colon\mathrm{Gal}(\overline{\mathbb Q}/\mathbb Q)\to\mathrm{GSp}_4$ via $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1 = \lambda_p$. | Chenevier 2014 (arXiv:1301.0635) pseudo-characters are a real substitute for genuine representations in Taylor-Wiles-style constructions; the SK-lift identity $\lambda_p(\Delta_{10}) = a_p(f_{16}) + p^8 + p^9$ is VERIFIED item 8 of the W19 adjudication ledger; a $4$-dim Galois representation of weight-motif $17$ attached to $\Delta_{10}$ is Taylor 1991 / Weissauer 2005 / Laumon 2005. | Type-confusion: Chenevier pseudo-characters live on COMMUTATIVE algebras mediating a profinite-group-to-representation datum (abstract Hecke algebras, completed group rings of $\mathrm{Gal}$); they are NOT defined on non-commutative chiral bialgebras. $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is a non-commutative $A_\infty$-quasi-Hopf chiral bialgebra (W15 item 17 of ledger); its natural "trace" is the BD chiral trace in the sense of Beilinson-Drinfeld 2004 Ch.4, which takes values in chiral modules and satisfies a factorisation-compatible identity, NOT the Chenevier symmetric-multiplicative-dimension axioms. Writing "$S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ on $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$" without the Hecke intermediary conflates a Chenevier pseudo-character on a commutative Hecke algebra with a chiral trace on a non-commutative chiral bialgebra. | Canonical source is the paramodular Hecke algebra $\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1$ at level $N=1$ (unique newform $\Delta_{10}\in S_{10}(K(1))^{\mathrm{new}}$ by Ibukiyama-Poor-Yuen 2019 IJNT 9 Thm 5.1; Poor-Schmidt-Yuen 2020 Exp Math 29). The $4$-dim $S^{\mathrm{ps}} = (S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1,\dots,S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4)\colon\mathbb T^{\mathrm{par}}_1\to\mathcal O_E\otimes\mathbb Z_\ell$ is given at Hecke generators $T_p$ by: $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1(T_p) = \lambda_p = a_p + p^8 + p^9$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_2(T_p,T_p) = \tfrac{1}{2}(\lambda_p^2 - \lambda_p(T_{p^2})) = p^{15} + (p^8+p^9)a_p + p^{17}$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_3(T_p,T_p,T_p) = a_p p^{17} + p^{23} + p^{24}$; $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4(T_p,T_p,T_p,T_p) = p^{32}$. The reciprocal spinor $L$-factor $\prod(1 - \alpha_i x) = 1 - S^{\mathrm{ps}}_1 x + S^{\mathrm{ps}}_2 x^2 - S^{\mathrm{ps}}_3 x^3 + S^{\mathrm{ps}}_4 x^4$ expands the SK-lift identity $L_p(s,\pi_{\Delta_{10}},\mathrm{spin}) = \zeta_p(s-8)\zeta_p(s-9)L_p(s,f_{16})$. Chenevier axioms (symmetry, multiplicativity, $S^{\mathrm{ps}}_5\circ\mathrm{Alt}_5 = 0$) are automatic from commutativity + Hecke multiplicativity + Cayley-Hamilton at $d = 4$. Deligne-Serre 1974 ENS 7 Sec 8 + Taylor 1991 Duke 63 Thm 2.1 extend $S^{\mathrm{ps}}$ to a genuine $\mathrm{GSp}_4(\mathcal O_E)$-valued Galois representation. Bridge to $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is via Satake-Frenkel-Gaitsgory chiralisation on the Koszul locus; chiral extension $S^{\mathrm{ps,ch}}\colon Z^{\mathrm{der}}_{\mathrm{ch}}(\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5})\to\mathcal O_E\otimes\overline{\mathbb Q}_\ell$ is CONJECTURAL. Verification on 22 primes $p \le 79$ via Hecke table (a_p from DELTA_E6_AP / DELTA_E6_AP_W17 in compute/lib/k3_yangian_wave14_arthur_hecke_delta10.py); Deligne bound $\vert a_p\vert \le 2p^{15/2}$ saturation peak 0.895 at $p = 37$ and 0.8575 at $p = 89$ (W18 extension). Inscription: Vol I chapters/theory/derived_langlands.tex Theorem thm:dl-wave19-pseudocharacter-delta10. Primary: Chenevier 2014 arXiv:1301.0635 Sec 1.2 Def/Prop 1.9; Taylor 1991 Duke 63 Thm 2.1; Weissauer 2005 LNM 1868 Sec 4; Laumon 2005 Publ IHES 102 Thm I.10; Deligne-Serre 1974 ASENS 7 Sec 8; Ikeda 2001 Ann Math 154 Cor 16.2; Andrianov 1974 Mat Sbornik 93 Prop 1.3.3; Gross 1998 Duke 91 (Satake transform); Ibukiyama-Poor-Yuen 2019 IJNT 9 Thm 5.1; Poor-Schmidt-Yuen 2020 Exp Math 29. | pseudocharacter-source-algebra-scope |
| W20-conway-vs-natural-psi-image-commutative-diamond | $V^{s\natural}$ is the 5th image of the universal $\Psi$-functor, on a separate lattice-input row from the four established rows (K3, Enriques, Monster, Fake-Monster), with lattice $\Lambda_{24}$ and parameters $(K, \hbar^2) = (2, -1/2)$ via a super-extension $K^{\mathrm{super}} = 2c_+(\Lambda_{24}\oplus\mathrm{II}_{1,1}^{\mathrm{super}}) = 2$ resolving the degeneracy $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 0$. | Duncan 2007 \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139, 255--315 (arXiv:math/0502267) constructs $V^{s\natural}$ as the unique self-dual $N{=}1$ SVOA of CFT type at $c = 12$ with $(V^{s\natural})_{1/2} = 0$ and $\mathrm{Aut} = \mathrm{Co}_0$; the construction is the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold $A(\Lambda_{24})^+\oplus A(\Lambda_{24})^{\mathrm{tw},+}$ of the $24$-generator fermionic vertex superalgebra attached to the Leech lattice. The commutative $\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifolding diamond $\{V_{\Lambda_{24}}, V^\natural, V_{\Lambda_{24}}^s, V^{s\natural}\}$ (Duncan 2007 \S6) is established; the four-row $\Psi$-landscape K3/Enriques/Monster/Fake-Monster is established. | Three concrete defects in the W19 Witten inscription (k3e_bkm_chapter.tex:4262 \emph{et seq.}): (a) journal venue stated as \emph{Math.\ Res.\ Lett.}~14 but correct venue is \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139 (task prompt's "arXiv:math/0605219" is a different Duncan paper; correct Conway arXiv is math/0502267); (b) construction described as "$\mathbb{Z}/2$-orbifold of 24 free fermions at the $E_8$ super-lattice tensored up" but Duncan 2007 \S3--4 uses the fermionic superalgebra $A(\Lambda_{24})$ on the Leech lattice---no $E_8$ super-lattice enters; (c) assignment $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 0$ contradicts the programme's universal sign convention (Theorem thm:bkm-universal-identity defines $c_+(L)$ as positive-eigenvalue count; Leech has signature $(24,0)$ so $c_+(\Lambda_{24}) = 24$, giving $K = 48$, $\hbar^2 = -1/48$, not $(2, -1/2)$). | The default W20 reading, consistent with the Duncan 2007 \S6 commutative orbifolding diamond, is that $V^{s\natural}$ is the $\mathbb{Z}/2$-super-twin of $V^\natural$ INSIDE the four-row $\Psi$-landscape (specifically the Monster row, via the diamond), NOT an independent fifth $\Psi$-image; $(K,\hbar^2) = (2,-1/2)$ coincides with Monster's because $V^{s\natural}$ inherits them from $V^\natural$ through the diamond. Alternative reading: Scheithauer 2008 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~172 Thm~3.2 realises $V^{s\natural}$ as a $\mathbb{Z}/2$-twisted subsector of the Fake-Monster row on $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ via $\Lambda_{24}\subset\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$. Cache discipline: $\Psi$ gives ONE output per input CATEGORY, so a VOA $V$ advertised as the image of two different $\Psi$-inputs is a symptom that the two inputs coincide under an orbifold-diamond / super-twin relation. Primary: Duncan 2007 \emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~139 arXiv:math/0502267 Thm 1.1, \S3--6; Duncan--Mack-Ono 2015 \emph{Forum Math.~Pi}~3 e10; Scheithauer 2008 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~172, 563--609 Thm 3.2; Borcherds 1998 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~132 Thm 13.3; FLM 1988 Ch.~12; Conway 1968 \emph{Bull.\ LMS}~1; Vol III chapters/examples/k3e_bkm_chapter.tex Conjecture conj:bkm-conway-psi-fifth-image and Remarks rem:bkm-conway-psi-image-sign-and-diamond, rem:bkm-conway-monster-fake-monster-triangle; notes/ADJUDICATION_LEDGER_WAVES_14_TO_19.md \S(III.B). | psi-image-vs-orbifold-diamond-twin |
| W19-grt1-BKM-transitivity-scope | $\mathfrak{grt}_1$ acts transitively on the full space $\mathrm{Quant}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5})$ of super-EK quantisations of the K3-BKM Lie superalgebra by Drinfeld twist, extending Etingof--Kazhdan 2000 Part V Thm 2.2 (affine KM) verbatim. | EK 2000 Part V Thm 2.2 establishes the affine case: $\mathrm{Quant}(\widehat{\mathfrak{g}}_{\mathrm{aff}})$ is a torsor over $\exp(\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1)$ under Drinfeld twist; $H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; V)$ vanishes for finite-rank affine modules $V$ (Willwacher 2015 Thm 1.1; Schnepper--Willwacher 2017). | The BKM imaginary cone is infinite-dimensional with Hardy--Ramanujan growth $\dim \mathrm{Imag}_N \sim N^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt N)$ (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Sec 4; A_infty-tower non-closure, ledger item I.17). Finite-rank EK Part V machinery does not extend verbatim: Drinfeld twist on the associator must converge in a weight-filtered pro-completion, and $H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; \widehat{\mathrm{Imag}})$ is not automatically vanishing. The super-quasi-Hopf sign contributes an additional $\mathbb{Z}/2$ factor (EK 2000 Part V Prop 2.1). | The correct transitivity statement is scope-restricted with an explicit obstruction cocycle. (a) Quantisation space: $\mathrm{Quant}^{\mathrm{GN}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5})$ = super-EK quantisations compatible with the Gritsenko--Nikulin automorphic denominator $e^\rho \prod_{\alpha \in \Delta_+^{\mathrm{im}}}(1-e^{-\alpha})^{\mathrm{mult}(\alpha)} = \sum_{w \in W}(-1)^{\ell(w)}w(e^\rho \Delta_5(e^{-\alpha}))$. (b) Obstruction: $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}} \in H^2(\mathfrak{grt}_1; \widehat{\mathrm{Imag}})$ with explicit cocycle $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}([f_a, f_b]) = \sum_{\alpha, \beta \in \Delta_+^{\mathrm{im}}} \langle \mathsf{g}_{a, b}, \alpha^\vee \otimes \alpha\rangle \cdot \mathrm{mult}(\alpha) \cdot [\alpha, \beta]_{\mathrm{Imag}}$, $\mathsf{g}_{a, b}$ the depth-2 Ihara bracket (Furusho 2011 Thm 4), $\mathrm{mult}(\alpha) = c_{K3}(4nm - \ell^2)$. (c) $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}$ vanishes on the Koszul locus $\overline{\mathcal{A}_2} \setminus \bigcup_{n \text{ admissible}} H_n$ (Theorem B, W18 Beilinson tightening, ledger II.E): bar--cobar is strict there, the motivic weight filtration on $\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1$ (Brown 2012) aligns with the Borcherds lattice-weight filtration on $\widehat{\mathrm{Imag}}$ via Deligne--Goncharov periods, and Schnepper--Willwacher 2017 graph-complex vanishing in positive depth applies. (d) The quotient $\mathrm{Quant}^{\mathrm{GN, Koszul}}(\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}) / (\mathbb{Z}/2)_{\mathrm{super}}$ by the EK super-sign is a torsor over $\exp(\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1)$. Unconditional through motivic weight 12 ($c_{12}^{(9)} = \zeta(3,3,3,3)/12!$ explicit, Vol I Rem rem:nc-wave19-DNA-c12-explicit); conditional on Zagier--Hoffman depth-reduction above weight 12 (ledger III.A). Three independent verification paths: (V1) affine limit recovers EK 2000 Part V exactly (imaginary cone vanishes on finite-rank affine sub-lattice); (V2) motivic-Galois pairing via Drinfeld--Deligne $\mathfrak{grt}_1 \cong \mathrm{Lie}(\pi_1^{\mathrm{mot, U}})$ gives chain-level numerical anchor at weight 12; (V3) Willwacher graph complex $H^0(\mathrm{GC}_2) = \mathfrak{grt}_1$ plus Schnepper--Willwacher 2017 extension to graph-complex-compatible modules. Primary: Drinfeld 1990 Leningrad J Math 1 Sec 5 Thm A'; Etingof--Kazhdan 2000 Sel Math 6 Part V Thm 2.2, Prop 2.1; Brown 2012 Ann Math 175 Thm 1.2; Willwacher 2015 Invent 200 Thm 1.1; Schnepper--Willwacher 2017; Furusho 2011 Ann Math 174 Thm 4; Kontsevich 2003 Lett Math Phys 66; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 AJM 119 Thm 4.1; Hardy--Ramanujan 1918. Main inscription: Vol III chapters/theory/quantum_groups_foundations.tex Sec sec:qgf-grt1-bkm Thm thm:qgf-grt1-bkm-transitivity Cor cor:qgf-grt1-affine-recovery Rem rem:qgf-grt1-three-paths; Vol I chapters/theory/nilpotent_completion.tex Rem rem:nc-grt1-bkm-transitivity-vol1. | grt1-BKM-Koszul-locus-obstruction-scope |
| W20-PBW-truncation-count-vs-multiplicity-collapse | At the Borcherds $\rho$-orbit $\mathcal{O}_N$ of the BKM $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}$ the PBW generator increment $d(N) - d(N-1)$ equals $|c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$ interpreted as the root-space dimension (multiplicity) of a single representative imaginary root at $\rho$-level $N$. | The K3 Fourier coefficient $c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta)$ computes BOTH (a) the root-space dimension $\dim\mathfrak{g}_\alpha = \mathrm{mult}(\alpha)$ for a fixed $\alpha$ with $-\alpha^2/2 = \Delta$ (Borcherds 1992 Thm.~10.1 exponent formula), AND (b) the $\rho^N$-coefficient in $\log\Delta_5$ which enumerates the orbit-integrated sum $\sum_{\alpha\in\mathcal{O}_N}\mathrm{mult}(\alpha)$ (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \S3 Thm.~3.1 denominator product). These are two DISTINCT numerical data that coincide only because the Borcherds denominator collapses the double-sum into a single K3 Fourier coefficient. | Conflating "count of positive roots at $\rho$-level $N$" with "multiplicity of a single root" at $\rho$-level $N$ is a category error. At $\rho$-level 1 for $\mathfrak{g}_{\Delta_5}$: three spacelike + one timelike real simple roots each of multiplicity $1$ (Feingold--Frenkel 1983, Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \S3, ledger VERIFIED item 4: signature $(2,1)$ Gram eigenvalues $\{+4,+4,-2\}$, four simples in total carrying the rank-3 real Cartan plus one hyperbolic); at imaginary $\rho$-levels $N \ge 2$, the increment $d(N) - d(N-1) = |c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$ is the sum-of-multiplicities over $\mathcal{O}_N$, not a raw root count. Writing "the two negative-norm imaginary generators at $\Delta = -1$" without distinguishing the two equivalent readings (two distinct roots $\times$ multiplicity $1$ vs one root $\times$ multiplicity $2$) is the kind of ambiguity that breaks the Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 PBW accounting downstream. Related AP: count-vs-sum-of-multiplicities. Sign convention trap: the Siegel-domain discriminant $\Delta = 4nm - \ell^2$ on $\Lambda^{2,1}_{II}$ and the Borcherds lattice norm convention $-\alpha^2/2$ agree on imaginary roots ($\alpha^2 \le 0$, $\Delta \ge 0$) but differ for real roots ($\alpha^2 = +2$, $\Delta = -1$): the polar $c_{\mathrm{K3}}(-1) = 2$ is the real-root orbit datum (orbit-count-times-multiplicity), NOT an imaginary root with norm $-2$. | Canonical formulation: at $\rho$-level $N$ the Lusztig-PBW exponent increment is $\Delta d(N) := \sum_{\alpha \in \mathcal{O}_N}\dim\mathfrak{g}_\alpha$, and the Borcherds--Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator product collapse identifies this with $|c_{\mathrm{K3}}(\Delta_N)|$. The full truncation dimension is then $\dim_{\mathbb{C}} \mathfrak{u}_{\zeta_8}^{\le N} = 8^{2 d(N) + \mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}}} = 8^{2 d(N) + 3}$, with $d(1) = 2$, $d(2) = 22$, $d(3) = 238$, $d(4) = 366$; the factor-of-2 in the exponent is the Lusztig-$E$/$F$-PBW split, not a count-vs-multiplicity ambiguity. Equivalent accounting $d^{\mathrm{alt}}(N) := 2 d(N)$ under the convention that the sum ranges over all of $\Phi^+ \cup \Phi^-$ recovers the task-prompt formula $8^{d^{\mathrm{alt}}(N) + 3}$; the two differ by a trivial factor of 2 bookkeeping, not by a genuine refinement. The $+3$ in the exponent is $\mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}} = 3$ (signature $(2,1)$, VERIFIED item 4), from the $K$-Cartan PBW slot. Primary: Lusztig 1993 \emph{Introduction to Quantum Groups} Birkh\"auser Ch.~35.1 Prop.~35.1.5; Borcherds 1992 \emph{Invent.}~109 Thm.~10.1 \S2.4; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 \emph{St.~Petersburg Math.~J.}~11 \S3 Thm.~3.1 eq.~2.4; Feingold--Frenkel 1983 \emph{Math.~Ann.}~263 Sec.~2; Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011 \texttt{arXiv:1004.0956} Tab.~1 ($c_{\mathrm{K3}}(-1) = 2, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(0) = 20, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(3) = 216, c_{\mathrm{K3}}(4) = -128$); Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 LMS LNS~262 \S2.3 Lemma~2.3.4. | W20-phi-n-13-16-Borcherds-MZV-ratio-exact-vs-asymptotic | The Borcherds/MZV leg ratio at $n=10,\ldots,16$ equals the bare Hardy--Ramanujan asymptotic $k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)/d_n$ with $k=\lceil n/2\rceil$, giving values $6.4\cdot 10^9$ at $n=10$ through $5\cdot 10^{13}$ at $n=16$. | The Borcherds leg $c^{(K3)}_n\Phi_{10}^{\lceil n/2\rceil}\eta^{-12n}/n!$ grows at Hardy--Ramanujan rate (Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Thm 1.5; Hardy--Ramanujan 1918), and the asymptotic functional form is correct. | The bare $k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ formula omits the Rademacher 1937 leading constant $(4\pi)^{-1}$ and overshoots the exact Fourier coefficient $p_{24}(k)=[q^k]\prod_m(1-q^m)^{-24}$ by a factor $\sim 10^2$ at $k\le 10$. At $k=5$ the asymptotic gives $6.1\cdot 10^6$ whereas $p_{24}(5)=176256$; the ratio $p_{24}(k)/d_n$ at $n=10$ is $35251$, not $6.4\cdot 10^9$. Conflation: asymptotic growth rate (load-bearing for divergence as $n\to\infty$) vs. numerical value at finite $n$ (load-bearing for the stated ratios; requires exact Fourier coefficient or Rademacher sum with subleading terms). | Canonical programme-values (exact, via $p_{24}(k)=[q^k]\prod_m(1-q^m)^{-24}$): $p_{24}(5)=176256$, $p_{24}(6)=1073720$, $p_{24}(7)=5930496$, $p_{24}(8)=30178575$; Padovan $d_{10},\ldots,d_{16}=5,7,9,12,16,21,28$; exact ratios $p_{24}(\lceil n/2\rceil)/d_n$ at $n=10,13,14,15,16$ are $3.53\cdot 10^4, 4.94\cdot 10^5, 3.71\cdot 10^5, 1.44\cdot 10^6, 1.08\cdot 10^6$. Asymptotic form with Rademacher prefactor $(4\pi)^{-1}k^{-27/4}\exp(4\pi\sqrt k)$ overshoots exact by $\sim 10^2$ at $k\le 10$. | W20-phi-n-leading-magnitude-offset-by-one | At weights $13,\ldots,16$ the MZV leg $\phi^{(n)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}$ has leading magnitudes $\sim 2\cdot 10^{-10}, 2\cdot 10^{-11}, 2\cdot 10^{-12}, 10^{-13}$. | The Brown canonical basis has $d_n$ entries at weight $n$ (Padovan $12,16,21,28$); each MZV $\zeta(s_1,\ldots,s_k)$ at weight $n\ge 10$ has value approaching $1$ (since $\zeta(n)\to 1$); the overall $1/n!$ normalisation divides by $6.2\cdot 10^9, 8.7\cdot 10^{10}, 1.3\cdot 10^{12}, 2.1\cdot 10^{13}$ for $n=13,\ldots,16$. | Leading-estimate $d_n\cdot 1/n!$ gives $\phi^{(13)}_{\mathrm{MZV}}\approx 12/(6.2\cdot 10^9)\approx 1.93\cdot 10^{-9}$, $\phi^{(14)}\approx 1.83\cdot 10^{-10}$, $\phi^{(15)}\approx 1.61\cdot 10^{-11}$, $\phi^{(16)}\approx 1.34\cdot 10^{-12}$. For $n\notin\{1,3,4\}$ the Bruinier Heegner--Chern torsion order $c_n$ is coprime to $\mathrm{lcm}(8,3,2)=24$ for first new cases ($c_7=14$ coprime to $48$; $c_8$ divides $16$ and adjoins new $\mathbb Z/16$ characters; $c_{11}=22$; $c_{15}=30$). Each admissible discriminant contributes a new $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triple to the CKS tower, not a specialisation of the $\{1,3,4\}$ triple; the pro-ambient index grows as an infinite direct sum $\bigoplus_{n\ \text{adm}}\mathfrak{sl}_2(H_n)$. Triple intersections $H_i\cap H_j\cap H_k$ are empty at codimension $3$ inside $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ (Igusa transversality); the deep-boundary Baily--Borel zero-cusp limit carries the countable joint nilpotent orbit. | The correct chain-level ambient on $\bigcup_{n\ \text{adm}}H_n$ is the bi-unipotent Malcev ladder $\bigcup_n F_n^{\mathrm{Malcev}}$ with pro-ambient index $(w,\{\chi_n\}_{n\ \text{adm}},\{k_n\}_{n\ \text{adm}})$, only finitely many $\chi_n\ne\chi_{0,n}$ per slot by the Gritsenko--Nikulin denominator vanishing order $\mathrm{ord}_{H_n}(\Delta_5)\ge\lceil n/24\rceil$. The named homotopy $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)} = \prod_{n\in S} M^{(\chi_n)}_{H_n}\circ (\sum_n N_n+\lambda_{\{k_n\}})^{-1}\circ(\mathrm{id}+\sigma h^{(g)})^{-1}\circ\sigma$ extends the hexachotomy to any finite admissible $S\supset\{1,3,4\}$, and the direct limit $\varinjlim_S h^{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)}$ recovers strict chain-level inversion on the full admissible union. The Baily--Borel zero-cusp specialisation $\lim_{\Im Z\to\infty}\Delta_5=\eta^{24}$ reduces the ladder to the $24$-power cusp residue by Schmid's multi-variable limit (Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986); every admissible discriminant contributes a new Malcev layer, not a specialisation. Inscribed in Vol~I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex as Theorem thm:mc5-admissible-heegner-strict-chain-level and Corollary cor:global-strict-admissible-heegner. Primary: Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Thm~1.1 + Prop~5.1 (admissible Heegner monodromy order); Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 Ann Math 123 Thm~3.3 \S 3.7 (multi-variable nilpotent-orbit commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triples); Saito 1988 Publ RIMS 24 Appendix~A Thm~A.3 (multi-variable $V$-filtration); Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Amer J Math 119 \S 3 Cor~3.2 (Siegel denominator vanishing order); Schmid 1973 Invent 22 \S 5 (limiting mixed Hodge structure at Baily--Borel cusp); Beilinson--Drinfeld 2004 Chiral Algebras \S 5.8 (pro-object compactness). | ambient-extension-by-new-data-per-admissible-n |

| W20-chirhoch-above-d-vanishes-coha-lean-mukai-pairing | Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA has non-zero Feigin--Odesskii generators $K_1, K_2, K_3, K_4, \ldots$ at every degree $n \ge 1$; the Mukai-pairing cocycles $\chi_n = \langle \mu_n^{\mathrm{CoHA}}(-), \Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}$ are non-zero for every $n$; so the Theorem~H concentration set $\{0,1,2,d\}$ is an amplitude bound, not a sharp vanishing statement. | CoHA richness is real: the generators $K_n$ are non-zero at every degree. The error is projecting CoHA richness to chiral Hochschild richness without tracking the Mukai-pairing filter. | Conflates CoHA-generator structure (rich at every degree in Feigin--Odesskii shuffle-presentation) with Mukai-pairing projection (top-degree-only by Caldararu 2005 \S4.2). The pairing $\langle -, \Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\mathrm{Muk}}$ vanishes identically on $H^p(\CY_d)$ for $p \neq 2d$; CoHA shuffle degree-additivity (Schiffmann--Vasserot 2013 Thm~6.1) places $\mu_n^{\CoHA}$ in cohomological degree $2n$; hence $\chi_n = 0$ at the pairing level for every $n \neq d$, regardless of non-vanishing of $\mu_n^{\CoHA}$. The CoHA is rich; the chiral Hochschild projection through $\Phi_d$ is lean. | Theorem~H concentration on $\Phi_d$-image is SHARP: $\ChirHoch^k_{\CY\text{-}d}(\Phi_d(\mathcal F)) = 0$ for every $k \notin \{0,1,2,d\}$. Sharpness established via three independent paths: (i) CoHA generator truncation (Mukai top-degree-only, Caldararu 2005 Adv Math 194 \S4.2); (ii) bar-spectral-sequence collapse at $E_2$ (Serre-parity $\Ext^p(\mathcal F, \mathcal F) = 0$ for $p > d$ on CY-$d$ via Caldararu 2005 Prop~2.1 + Huybrechts--Thomas 2010 Math Ann 346 Prop~2.3); (iii) reduced DT--Betti vanishing on K3$\times E$ (Oberdieck 2018 Geom \& Topol 22 \S5.4: $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$ Fourier--Jacobi expansion has non-zero Betti coefficients only in $g\in\{1,2,3\}$; Maulik--Oberdieck--Pandharipande 2017 arXiv:1605.05473 Thm~1 reduced DT cap). | W21-8-to-129-is-Borel-sub-Hopf-not-full-small-form | The exponent $8^{129}$ in $\dim\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}(\widehat{\mathfrak m}_{\Delta_5})$ is the dimension of a filtered Hopf quotient $\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N_\star}$ of the full Lusztig small form at some intermediate height $N_\star$ between $N=2$ and $N=3$, obtainable by restricting the height-$3$ orbit $\mathcal O_3$ of multiplicity $|c_{\mathrm K3}(3)|=216$ to a partial $M_{24}$-invariant generator set of size $41$. | The cumulative PBW count $d(N)$ of Proposition~\texttt{prop:qgf-truncation-dims} is genuinely well-defined, strictly monotone, and indexed by the admissible Borcherds discriminants $\Delta_N\in\{-1,0,3,4,7,8,\ldots\}$ with $d(N)-d(N-1)=|c_{\mathrm K3}(\Delta_N)|$; the number $8^{129}$ really does appear in the programme. | Conflates two DISTINCT mathematical objects sharing the same numerical exponent $129$: (a) the full two-sided small-form truncation $\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N}$ of dimension $\ell^{2d(N)+\mathrm{rank}_{\mathrm{real}}}$ with $d(N)\in\{2,22,238,366,\ldots\}$ and exponents $\in\{7,47,479,735,\ldots\}$, which SKIPS $129$ by arithmetic gap; (b) the positive-Borel sub-Hopf-algebra $\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}$ of the real-root saturation, of dimension $\ell^{|\Phi^{\mathrm{real}}_+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{129}$ exactly. The filtration-quotient interpretation is BLOCKED by two obstructions: (i) arithmetic — $d(N)=63$ has no integer solution in $\{0,2,22,238,366,\ldots\}$; (ii) $M_{24}$-equivariance — the $216$ generators at $\Delta_3=3$ form a single moonshine orbit whose $M_{24}$-decomposition $\{1,23,45,231,252,\ldots\}$ has no cumulative sum equal to the required $41$. Hence $8^{129}$ CANNOT be realised as $\dim\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\le N_\star}$ for any filtered truncation height $N_\star$, integer or partial-$M_{24}$-invariant. | The sharp reinterpretation: $8^{129}$ is a BOREL-SUB-HOPF dimension and a MODULAR-CATEGORY PROJECTIVE-INDEX cardinality, not a filtered small-form Hopf-quotient dimension. Specifically, $\dim\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}=\ell^{|\Phi^{\mathrm{real}}_+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{126+3}=8^{129}$ (Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 Prop.~35.1.5 applied to the positive-half Borel of the rank-$3$ real-root Coxeter subsystem), and $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|_{\mathrm{KL\,MTC}}=8^{129}$ (Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 LMS LNS~262 \S6 Thm.~6.2.1: cardinality of the indecomposable-projective index set of the non-semisimple modular tensor category $\mathrm{Rep}^{\mathrm{fd}}(\mathfrak u_{\zeta_8}^{\mathrm{re}})$ at level $\ell=8$). Every future statement invoking $8^{129}$ must name which invariant is meant: (a) $\dim\mathfrak b^{\mathrm{re},+}_{\zeta_8}$ (Borel sub-Hopf dimension), (b) $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|$ (KL projective-index cardinality), or (c) $|\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}/8\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}|_{\mu_8\text{-gerbe}}$ (Bruinier-twisted section count on the real-root sublattice). Three verification paths: (P1) Lusztig 1993 Ch.~35.1 positive-half PBW count $\ell^{N+r}=8^{126+3}$; (P2) Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 \S6 Thm.~6.2.1 non-semisimple-MTC projective-index formula $|\Lambda|=\ell^{|\Phi^+|+\mathrm{rank}}=8^{129}$; (P3) Bruinier 2002 LNM~1780 Prop.~5.1 $\mu_8$-gerbe-twisted section count on the rank-$129$ real-root sublattice $\Lambda^{\mathrm{re}}\subset\mathrm{II}_{4,20}$, matched to the lattice-Hopf correspondence of Scheithauer 2009 \emph{Adv.~Math.}~225 \S4.2. All three agree at $8^{129}$; none attach it to a full small-form truncation. Primary: Lusztig 1993 \emph{Introduction to Quantum Groups} Ch.~35.1 Prop.~35.1.5 (PBW triangular factor); Kerler--Lyubashenko 2001 LMS LNS~262 \S6 Thm.~6.2.1 (non-semisimple MTC projective index); Bruinier 2002 LNM~1780 Prop.~5.1 ($\mu_\ell$-gerbe obstruction); Eguchi--Ooguri--Tachikawa 2011 \emph{Exp.~Math.}~20 Table~1 ($c_{\mathrm K3}$ Fourier coefficients); Cheng--Duncan--Harvey 2014 \emph{Res.~Math.~Sci.}~1 \S2 (Mathieu moonshine $M_{24}$-decomposition of $\phi_{0,1}^{\mathrm K3}$); Gritsenko--Hulek 1998 \emph{Internat.~J.~Math.}~9 Table~1 ($|\Phi^{\mathrm{real}}_+(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})|=126$); Scheithauer 2009 \emph{Adv.~Math.}~225 \S4.2 (lattice-Hopf/theta correspondence). | W21-compat-homotopy-choice-vs-torsor-over-Aut_Linfty | The compatibility homotopy $h_\square$ of Theorem \texttt{thm:mc5-compatibility-square} is a chosen element of the set $\mathcal C_\square(A)$ of degree-$(-1)$ fillings of the square $(\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{Malcev}})=[d,-]$; different fillings correspond to different mathematical content, so the hexachotomy datum depends on the choice. | The square admits at least one canonical filling $h_\square$ exhibited in the proof of \texttt{thm:mc5-compatibility-square}; two fillings differ by a closed degree-$(-1)$ element. | Conflates set-level choice with $\infty$-groupoid-level canonicity. Higher simplicial levels are classified by $H^{-k}\mathrm{Def}=\pi_k B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}$. The correct question is not "which filling" but "what is the $\infty$-groupoid $\mathsf{Data}(A)$ of all fillings together with coherent homotopies up the Dold--Kan tower". Conflation risks (a) treating $h_\square$ as a structural constant, (b) missing the torsor identification with $B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}$, (c) misreading the hexachotomy as a menu of choices rather than a canonical datum. | Canonical reciprocity statement: $\mathsf{Data}(A)\simeq B\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$ where $\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)=\exp(H^0\mathrm{Def}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A))\ltimes K(H^{<0}\mathrm{Def},\cdot)$ is the derivation-exponential $\infty$-group; any two fillings are connected by a canonical path, and $\pi_k\mathsf{Data}(A)=H^{-k}\mathrm{Def}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$. Contractibility criterion: $\mathsf{Data}(A)$ contractible iff $H^{\bullet\le 0}\mathrm{Def}=0$, equivalently iff $\mathrm{Aut}^h_{L_\infty}(\mathfrak g^{\infty,1}_A)$ is contractible. For $A=\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$: $H^0\mathrm{Def}\cong\widehat{\mathfrak{grt}}_1/\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{GN}}$ (cache entry \texttt{W19-grt1-BKM-transitivity-scope}), non-trivial on the Koszul locus $\overline{\mathcal A_2}\setminus\bigcup_{n\,\mathrm{adm}}H_n$; contractibility holds only on the affine sub-locus where the imaginary cone collapses. Reciprocity consequence: the hexachotomy entry of Vol I Thm \texttt{thm:mc5-infty-one-obstruction-tower} and the heptachotomy of Vol II Part \texttt{part:platonic-seven-faces} are canonical mathematical data, not menus of choices. | W20-infty-one-obstruction-tower-single-ext2-vs-massey-tower | The $(\infty,1)$-bar-cobar inversion on $\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})$ is controlled by the single Yoneda-$\mathrm{Ext}^2$ class $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A\in\mathrm{Ext}^2_{\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})}(A,A^!)$; its vanishing is necessary and sufficient for $\Omega^{\mathrm{ch}}B^{\mathrm{ch}}(A)\simeq A$ in the factorisation $\infty$-category. | The $\mathrm{Ext}^2$ class is real, is the primary Kadeishvili Massey class $\mathrm{ob}^{(2)}_A=[l_2]$, and is necessary for $(\infty,1)$-inversion. | Collapses the full Massey-tower coherence obligation of Lurie HA \S5.2.7 (lax counit) to a single primary class. Hexachotomy entry (6) $\mathrm{Perf}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})$ is now concrete; entries (1)--(5) absorb sub-towers.
