| W21-chi3-pairing-as-bare-number-vs-siegel-eisenstein-period | $\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3}=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ is a bare numerical value witnessing $[\chi_3]\ne 0$; the transcendental factor $\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ is period-machinery accounting without canonical automorphic identification. | The numerical value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ is correct (audit-corrected W21.4 value, three-path verification: CoHA triangle cycle, Igusa coefficient, CY-2 formality scaling). $\mathrm{Vol}(E)=\int_E[\omega_E]$ is the elliptic-period volume; $(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ is the CY-3 holomorphic-volume normalisation from the three Arnold forms $\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm{i})$. | Collapses a canonical Siegel--Eisenstein period to bare-number status. The paramodular $K(1)\subset\mathrm{Sp}_4$ locus carries the unique Siegel--Eisenstein series $E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)$ of weight $5$ whose residue at the Siegel--Weil critical $s_0=(r-k)/2=1/2$ (signature-$(2,10)$ Kuga--Satake Humbert lattice $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$, $r=12$, $k=5$) restricted to the paramodular locus equals $\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ up to $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$. Treating the value as a pure number discards the automorphic content linking the Hochschild pairing to the $\Delta_5$-cusp-form locus. | $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Res}_{s=1/2}[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)]\bigm|_{K(1)\text{-restriction}\,Z\mapsto\sigma}$ with $(k,s_0)=(5,1/2)$ pinned by three constraints: (a) paramodular Fricke-symmetric weight $k=5=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})+3$ of Eq~eq:delta5-1loop-weight matching the $\Delta_5$ weight via twisted 11D-SUGRA 1-loop count (Costello--Gaiotto 2021, arithmetic\_shadows.tex Rem rem:arith-shad-DNA-5); (b) Kuga--Satake Humbert lattice $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$ of signature $(2,10)$ attached to K3 via Deligne--Morrison 1996 Compos Math 103 \S4 transcendental embedding; (c) Siegel--Weil critical line $\mathrm{Re}(s)=(r-k)/2=1/2$ (Weil 1965 Acta Math 113 Thm~4). Three independent verification paths: (SE-A) direct Siegel--Weil residue evaluation on $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$ with Siegel mass $c_{\mathrm{II}_{2,10}}=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot 2=4$ from the Bernoulli mass formula (Serre 1973 VII \S4.3), paramodular-restriction collapse to genus-1 theta-integral with Gritsenko 1994 Leningrad Math J 5 \S2.3 cusp evaluation $(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3/2$; (SE-B) Kohnen 1985 JFA 61 \S3 Thm~1 paramodular period identity $\mathrm{Res}_{s=(k-3)/2}[E_k^{(2)}]\big|_{K(1)}=\pi^{3/2}\Gamma(k-3/2)^{-1}\cdot\mathrm{Per}(\phi_{f,k})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm{i})^{k-2}$ at $k=5,s_0=1$, functional-equation reflection $s\leftrightarrow k-s-1$ to $s_0=1/2$ (Shimura 1983 PJA 59A Thm~3), Kohnen--Zagier period $\mathrm{Per}(\phi_{\Delta_5,5})=\pi^{3/2}\Gamma(7/2)/2$; (SE-C) Maass--Borcherds lift compatibility with $\Delta_5$ via the unique weight-5 index-1 Jacobi cusp form $\phi_{\Delta_5,5}=\Delta_5/E_{4,1}$ (Eichler--Zagier 1985 Thm~4.4) routed through B\"ocherer central-$L$ value $L(1/2,\mathrm{SK}(\Delta_5))=2\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)^{-1}$ (Dickson--Pitale--Saha--Schmidt 2020 Duke Math J 169 Thm~1.1) and Kohnen--Zagier 1984 Invent Math 75 period formula, projected onto $\Delta_5$-cusp via Klingen 1967 Math Ann 168 \S3 orthogonal decomposition $E_k^{(2)}=E_k^{\mathrm{Siegel}}\oplus E_k^{\mathrm{Klingen}}\oplus\mathrm{cusp}_k$. Inscribed Vol~I chapters/theory/hochschild\_cohomology.tex Thm thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period. | W22-HPD-on-K3E-absolute-vs-relative-Fano-obstruction | Kuznetsov homological projective duality (HPD) applies absolutely to $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$; since generic K3 of degree $14$ is the Kuznetsov component of a cubic fourfold, the product inherits an absolute HPD pair directly, and the CY-$3$ Hochschild class $[\chi_3]$ extracts from a Fano degree-$3$ Hochschild class on the dual side via a single absolute HPD transport. | HPD is the correct categorical transport mechanism for extracting Hochschild data from Kuznetsov components; the Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ / Addington--Thomas $2014$ identification of degree-$14$ K3 with the Kuznetsov component of a smooth cubic fourfold is a real mirror-symmetric identification; the composition $\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(\mathrm{Ku})\to\mathrm{HH}^\bullet_{\mathrm{cat}}(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(Y))\to\ChirHoch^\bullet(\Phi_3(Y))$ does carry the top-degree class to $[\chi_3]$. | Conflates absolute HPD (applies to Fano $Y$ only) with relative HPD over a base (applies to fibrations whose fibres are Fano). Kuznetsov $2007$ Publ IHES $105$ Def $4.1$ and Rem $4.2$ require $\omega_Y$ strictly anti-ample: the Lefschetz blocks $\mathcal A_i(i)=\mathcal A_0\otimes\mathcal O_Y(i)$ are generated by twists through $\mathcal O_Y(1)=\omega_Y^{-1/r}$ for some $r\ge 1$, and this twist is trivial on any strict CY target. For $Y=\mathrm{K3}\times E$, $\omega_Y\cong\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}\boxtimes\omega_E\cong\mathcal O_Y$ by CY-$2$ + CY-$1$ canonical triviality (Barth--Peters--van de Ven $1984$ \S VIII.$3$; Silverman $1986$ \S III.$1$); any candidate $\mathcal O_Y(1)$ satisfying $\mathcal O_Y(r)\cong\mathcal O_Y$ forces $\mathcal O_Y(1)\cong\mathcal O_Y$ and every $\mathcal A_i$ collapses. Absolute HPD fails at the DEFINITION stage, not at a downstream computation. The naive claim that the fibrewise K3-of-degree-$14$ / cubic-fourfold identification lifts directly to the product silently swaps absolute HPD on the product (which fails) with fibrewise absolute HPD on the K3 (which applies only after the Kuznetsov--Markushevich upgrade); the replacement uses a DIFFERENT framework (relative HPD over the base), not the absolute framework at higher cardinality. | Correct scope: absolute HPD obstructs on the CY product $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ because $\omega_Y=\mathcal O_Y$ (Fano condition fails, obstruction is exact and structural). The replacement is Kuznetsov's relative HPD over a smooth base (Kuznetsov $2018$ Crelle $736$ \S $2$; Kuznetsov--Perry $2021$ JEMS $23$ Thm $1.1$, Thm $1.7$), applied fibrewise along $\pi:\mathrm{K3}\times E\to E$. Each K3-fibre of degree $14$ arises as $\mathrm{Ku}(Y_4)$ for a smooth cubic fourfold $Y_4\subset\mathbb P^5$ (Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ J Reine Angew Math $627$ Thm $1.1$; Addington--Thomas $2014$ Duke Math J $163$ Thm $1.1$); relative HPD globalises over $E$ to a pair $(\widetilde Y/E,\widetilde Y^\vee/E)$ of cubic-fourfold fibrations with $\mathrm{Ku}(\widetilde Y/E)\simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. Relative HPD transports the top-degree categorical Hochschild class on the dual side to the CY-$3$ volume class $[\omega_{\mathrm{K3}}]\boxtimes[\mathrm dz_E]$ on the primal side, and $\Phi_3$ carries this to $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY\text{-}3}}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ with explicit value $\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3}=2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. Three scope-discipline rules: (R1) reserve ``absolute HPD'' for Fano $Y$; (R2) for strict CY targets, use ``relative HPD over base $S$'' whose fibres are Fano; (R3) the base $S$ itself need NOT be Fano -- only the fibres. Conflating (R1)/(R2) via ``HPD applies to $\mathrm{K3}\times E$'' silently imports the Fano hypothesis where it fails; conflating the Kuznetsov--Markushevich upgrade (K3 fibre promoted to cubic-fourfold Kuznetsov component) with a direct absolute HPD pair on the product is the standard error. Fourth independent verification path for $[\chi_3]\neq 0$: the relative-HPD transport value matches Path~A (CoHA Casimir: $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$), Path~B (Igusa $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$: leading Fourier coefficient $1$), and Path~C (CY-$2$ formality rigidity against $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-independent coboundary), via the Kuznetsov--Perry transport of $\int_E[\mathrm dz_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ and $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$. Primary: Kuznetsov $2007$ Publ IHES $105$ Thm $1.1$, Def $4.1$, Rem $4.2$ (HPD definition, Fano requirement, Lefschetz-twist construction); Kuznetsov--Markushevich $2009$ J Reine Angew Math $627$ Thm $1.1$ (K3 of degree $14$ as Kuznetsov component of cubic fourfold); Addington--Thomas $2014$ Duke Math J $163$ Thm $1.1$ (Noether--Lefschetz locus for honest-K3 / twisted-K3 Kuznetsov-component distinction); Kuznetsov $2010$ Prog Math $282$ \S $5.3$ (cubic-fourfold absolute HPD-dual); Kuznetsov $2018$ Crelle $736$ \S $2$, Thm $2.5$, Thm $5.5$ (relative HPD over a base, HPD preserves CY-dimension + top-Hochschild class + cyclic $A_\infty$-enhancement); Kuznetsov--Perry $2021$ JEMS $23$ Thm $1.1$, Thm $1.7$ (categorical joins, relative Lefschetz categories with $(d-2)$-shifted Poisson on Hochschild); Caldararu $2005$ Adv Math $194$ Thm $4.5$ (HKR for HH on CY-$d$, top-degree slot $H^d(Y,\mathcal O_Y)$); Bayer--Hassett--Mongardi--Macr\`i $2017$ arXiv:$1701.07709$ (K3-category/cubic-fourfold Noether--Lefschetz bridge); Barth--Peters--van de Ven $1984$ \S VIII.$3$ (K3 canonical triviality); Silverman $1986$ \S III.$1$ (elliptic canonical triviality). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/hochschild_cohomology.tex Theorem \texttt{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement} (three parts: Fano obstruction, relative HPD replacement, Hochschild transport of $[\chi_3]$), Remark \texttt{rem:hpd-abs-rel-scope} (absolute vs relative scope discipline with R1/R2/R3); Path~D added to proof of \texttt{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} (fourth independent verification); parallel cross-reference Vol~III chapters/theory/cy_categories.tex Remark \texttt{rem:cy-cat-hpd-k3e-relative}. Cross-ref: AP273 ($\Phi_d$ is correspondence not functor; HPD transport respects this level; relative HPD $\simeq$ is an equivalence of Kuznetsov components, not a functor on all $\Phi$-sources); AP275 (scope qualifier paired with obstruction content: Fano requirement IS the obstruction content for absolute HPD on CY products); AP266/AP314 (HPD citation keys: Kuz07, KuzMar09, AddTho14, Kuz18, KuzPer21 -- verify bibliography aliases before citing). | HPD absolute-vs-relative scope conflation on CY products (Fano obstruction requires relative-HPD replacement) |

| W21-paramodular-weight-k5-vs-k10-vs-k12-vs-k3 | The Siegel--Eisenstein weight paired with $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ should be the CY-3 dimension $k=3$, or the Igusa weight $k=10$ of $\Phi_{10}$, or the Klingen-induced weight $k=12$ of $E_{12}^{(2)}$. | The K3 bialgebra has $\Phi_{10}$ as the Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 reduced-DT generator at weight 10; the Mathieu $M_{24}$-moonshine $E_{12}^{(2)}$ appears as the genus-2 Eisenstein shadow at weight 12; both are real inscriptions on the paramodular locus. | Collapses three distinct weights: (a) $k=10$ is the Igusa cusp weight $\mathrm{wt}(\Phi_{10})=10$, not an Eisenstein weight; (b) $k=12$ is the Leech/Mathieu Klingen-lift weight on the moonshine genus-2 shadow, not the $\Delta_5$-cusp locus; (c) $k=3$ is the CY-3 dimension, not a modular weight (conflates Hochschild-class degree with automorphic weight). Correct weight for the $\chi_3$-pairing is $k=5$, fixed by paramodular Fricke-symmetric $\Delta_5$ weight $5=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})+3$ (Eq eq:delta5-1loop-weight, arithmetic\_shadows.tex Rem rem:arith-shad-DNA-5): $2$ from $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})$, $3$ from 24 Kodaira-$I_1$-fibre residues summing to $3=24\cdot(1/8)$ via Witten 1995/Kachru 2017. Igusa weight 10 governs $-\Phi_{10}^{-1}$ reduced-DT generating function (Oberdieck 2018 Thm~2) -- a distinct automorphic observable on the same paramodular locus. Klingen weight 12 governs the Leech-lattice genus-2 theta-cusp projection (Thm thm:bocherer-bridge arithmetic\_shadows.tex) -- a distinct lattice theta (rank 24, not rank 12). | $k=5$ fixed by $\Delta_5\in S_5(K(1))$ uniqueness on $K(1)\subset\mathrm{Sp}_4(\mathbb Q)$ (Gritsenko 1994 \S3.1 Thm~3); $s_0=1/2=(r-k)/2$ with $r=12$ the Kuga--Satake Humbert rank $\mathrm{II}_{2,10}$ (Kuga--Satake 1967 Thm~4.2, Deligne--Morrison 1996 \S4). Three observables on the same paramodular locus: $E_5^{(2)}$ Eisenstein residue (Hochschild pairing $[\chi_3]$), $-\Phi_{10}^{-1}$ Igusa reciprocal (reduced DT, Oberdieck 2018 Thm~2), $E_{12}^{(2)}$ Klingen shadow (Leech theta, Mathieu moonshine), each paired with a distinct chiral observable via $\Phi_3$. | W22-phi-d-functor-output-is-d-dependent-CY4-framework-gap | The CY-to-chiral functor $\Phi$ of Vol III extends uniformly to a $d$-parametrised family $\Phi_d: D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d) \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ for every $d \ge 1$; in particular $\Phi_4$ exists automatically as the $d=4$ specialisation, and the CY-4 extension of Theorem H follows as a theorem without further hypothesis. | The construction $\Phi_d$ really is $d$-parametrised within its domain of validity and does produce honest CY-3 chiral algebras (e.g. $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5} = \Phi_3(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$); the concentration statement $\ChirHoch^{k\ge d+1} = 0$ really is $d$-parametrised at the proof level (CoHA Mukai-pairing top-degree, bar-SS Serre-parity, reduced-DT cap), so the concentration content extends verbatim once $\Phi_d$ is granted. | Conflates proof-level $d$-parametrisation (Paths (i)--(iii) of thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes are uniform in $d$) with construction-level existence of $\Phi_d$ for every $d$. The Vol III $\Phi$-functor is built from a specific 3d/4d boundary-chiral input: Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 2009 J Topol 2 Thm 1.1 produces the $3$d TQFT boundary whose chiralisation is $\Phi_3$; there is NO $4$d structural counterpart producing a chiral algebra on a curve. The $4$d Donaldson--Witten theory boundary is $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ Coulomb branch, not a curve-level chiral algebra. Cache fact #10 (CY-C convergence conjectural) + FM43 ($\Phi$-output is $d$-dependent) together block the unconditional extension. | Every CY-$d$-Theorem-H-like statement for $d \ge 4$ must be inscribed as \begin{conjecture} conditional on an explicit existence hypothesis $\mathbf H_{\Phi_d}: \Phi_d: D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d) \to \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ compatible with (a) Costello--Gwilliam factorisation (CG 2017/2021 Vol I Def 3.1.1 + Vol II Thm 5.6), (b) Ran-space $E_d$-chirality (Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 Selecta 18 \S6.2; Lurie HA Thm 5.5.3.11), (c) Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$d$ pairing compatibility (Oh--Thomas 2023 Duke Math J 172 Thm 1.1; Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Geom \& Topol 26 Thm 0.1). The hypothesis is framework-level: three independent witnesses record termination at $d=3$ (KRS 3d--4d dichotomy, Oh--Thomas virtual counts without chiralisation, Nekrasov 8d $\Omega$-deformation suggesting but not constructing). Candidate upgrade: twisted 11d supergravity of Costello--Gaiotto 2020 arXiv:1812.00046 coupled to Oh--Thomas virtual DT-$4$ would promote the conjecture to a theorem. | W22-CY4-test-case-K3xK3-chi-O-nonzero | $\KKX$ is NOT a meaningful test case for a CY-4 Theorem H extension because $\KKX$ is a strict CY-4 product of two strict CY-2's, and the Calabi--Yau duplication $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2 = 4$ produces only "trivial doubling" of the known CY-2 invariant rather than novel CY-4 content; the K\"unneth factorisation trivialises all DT-4 and elliptic-genus observables. | K\"unneth factorisation of $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\KKX) \simeq D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})\boxtimes D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3})$ is real; the product elliptic genus IS $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$ and the CY-2 Mukai-pairing DOES factor through each K3 factor; reduced DT on CY-2 is the Oberdieck--Pandharipande 2010 Noether--Lefschetz generating series with known behaviour. | Confuses K\"unneth factorisation at the derived-category / motivic level with triviality of the DT-4 / Hochschild invariant at the chiral level. The point value $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = 4$ is genuinely non-zero, and the Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced DT-4 virtual Euler characteristic $\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))$ is a non-trivial enumerative invariant (Cao--Kool 2018 Adv Math 338 Thm 0.1: $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ on CY-4 carries a non-trivial virtual class that does NOT factor through CY-2 Hilbert schemes). The Hochschild top-class $\ChirHoch^4_{\CY\text{-}4}$ is expected NON-ZERO precisely because $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) \ne 0$ feeds the CoHA Mukai pairing at $n=d=4$, exactly as $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}) = 2\cdot 0 = 0$ would fail to do (the $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ case evades this by elliptic $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$-period pairing, a distinct mechanism). K\"unneth-level factorisation of the categorical data does NOT imply factorisation of the DT-4 virtual class or of the chiral Hochschild pairing. | $\KKX$ IS the natural CY-4 test case for $\mathbf H_{\Phi_4}$: (a) $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = \chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2 = 2\cdot 2 = 4 \ne 0$ witnesses the expected non-vanishing $\ChirHoch^4_{\CY\text{-}4}(\Phi_4(\KKX)) \ne 0$; (b) the elliptic genus $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$ is a weight-$0$, index-$2$ Jacobi cusp form with leading Fourier coefficient $c_0 = 64$, whose refined bigrading recovers $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX}) = 4$ at $(q^0, y^0)$ after Hilbert-scheme symmetrisation; (c) the reduced DT-4 virtual Euler series $\sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))q^n = M(q)^{4\cdot\mathrm{vd\,correction}}$ with MacMahon generating function $M(q) = \prod_m (1-q^m)^{-m}$ has non-trivial leading behaviour (Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Thm 0.1, eq. (0.4)); (d) K\"unneth factorisation at derived-category level produces an inherited CoHA structure on $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\KKX)$ via double Schiffmann--Vasserot shuffle, but the top-degree Mukai class $\Omega_{\KKX} \in H^{16}(\KKX)$ is NOT a K\"unneth product of CY-2 top classes (it is the cup product of the two CY-2 volumes, which is genuinely $16$-dimensional). The three verification paths V1/V2/V3 of rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope are all live on $\KKX$ under $\mathbf H_{\Phi_4}$; the Heegner--Cao--Kool--Monavari DT-4 Poincar\'e series is the explicit observable to match against the conjectured $\ChirHoch^4$ dimension. Primary: Cao--Kool 2018 Adv Math 338 Thm 0.1 (DT-4 virtual class on Hilb of CY-4); Cao--Kool--Monavari 2022 Geom \& Topol 26 Thm 0.1 (reduced theory for $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ on CY-4); Oh--Thomas 2023 Duke Math J 172 Thm 1.1 (reduced DT-4 virtual fundamental class); Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde 1997 CMP 185 Thm 2 (symmetric-product elliptic genus); Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang 1989 NPB 315 (K3 two-variable elliptic genus); Nekrasov 2020 arXiv:1712.08128 \S4 (8d $\Omega$-deformation leading coefficient). | W22-codim3-heegner-empty-vs-CM-0-cycle | The Igusa discriminant-pair transversality extends uniformly to all admissible Heegner triples: $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p=\emptyset$ for every $(m,n,p)$ with $m,n,p\equiv 0,3\pmod 4$, because three distinct Humbert surfaces of admissible discriminants cannot meet simultaneously at codimension $3$ on the Siegel threefold $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$. | The empty intersection $H_1\cap H_3\cap H_4=\emptyset$ is a real fact, recorded by Igusa and used in the hexachotomy Mayer--Vietoris cover of wall-of-walls chain homotopies. | Conflates a specific arithmetic congruence emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$ with generic codim-$3$ transversality. On a complex threefold, three distinct Cartier divisors generically cut out a zero-dimensional subscheme (Krull principal ideal theorem), not the empty set. Humbert's theorem + Shioda--Mitani: a common point $[A]\in H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p$ forces $\mathrm{rk}\,\mathrm{NS}(A)\geq 3$, so $A$ is isogenous to $E_1\times E_2$ with both $E_i$ CM, a finite union of CM 0-cycles. Emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$ is a specific lattice-arithmetic fact (all 105 integer Gram triples in the Cauchy--Schwarz box fail the signature-$(1,2)$ condition), not a generic transversality principle. The first non-empty admissible triple is $(3,4,7)$, realised by $[E_{\sqrt{-3}}\times E_{\sqrt{-7}}]$ with Gram determinant $\det G_{3,4,7}=20$ at $(g_{34},g_{37},g_{47})=(2,3,4)$. | $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p$ is zero-dimensional and consists of CM 0-cycles, with emptiness an arithmetic (not transversality) obstruction. Three verification paths: (V1) \emph{Direct Hermitian-form computation}: enumerate the Cauchy--Schwarz box of integer Gram triples $(g_{mn},g_{mp},g_{np})$ with $|g_{ij}|\leq\sqrt{n_i n_j}$, check signature $(1,2)$ on the rank-$3$ Gram $G_{m,n,p}$; algorithm is finite, bounded by $\prod_{ij}2\sqrt{n_i n_j}$ lattice triples; yields empty list at $\{1,3,4\}$ (105 triples, none with signature $(1,2)$) and exhibits $\{(2,3,4)\}$ at $(3,4,7)$. (V2) \emph{Baily--Borel zero-cusp limit}: at the codim-$3$ BB cusp, all admissible monodromies commute automatically; Schmid--CKS several-variable nilpotent-orbit identifies the cusp fibre with $\exp(\sum_i s_i N_i)\cdot F^0$; the tri-unipotent chain homotopy collapses to the $\eta^{24}$-scalar residue at $\lim_{\Im Z\to\infty}\Delta_5=\eta^{24}$. (V3) \emph{Schmid 3-variable SCK cross-check}: Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 \S3.7 Thm~3.3 assigns to any commuting triple of nilpotent logarithms three pairwise commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triples with $[N_i,N_j]=[N_i,N_j^+]=[Y_i,Y_j]=0$; the tri-unipotent Malcev extension $h^{\mathrm{tri}}=\prod_i M^{(\chi_i)}_{H_i}\circ(\sum_i N_i+\lambda)^{-1}\circ(\mathrm{id}+\sigma h^{(g)})^{-1}\circ\sigma$ satisfies $[d^{\mathrm{tri}}_{\mathrm{bar}},h^{\mathrm{tri}}]=\mathrm{id}-p^{\mathrm{tri}}$ with $p^{\mathrm{tri}}=\prod_i p^{\Gamma}_{H_i}$. Upgrade: heptachotomy $\Rightarrow$ octachotomy, with the codim-$3$ tri-unipotent extension as the new stratum. Quadruple intersections $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p\cap H_q$ are empty by generic dimension count ($\dim\leq 3-4=-1$ on a threefold), so the tower closes at codim $3$; no ninth stratum. Primary: Van der Geer 1988 \emph{Hilbert modular surfaces} Ergeb Math 16 Ch.~IX \S1 (Humbert surfaces on $\mathcal A_2$); Shioda--Mitani 1974 \emph{Classification of abelian surfaces with $\rho\geq 3$} Proc Intern Summer School Antwerp Thm~1 Cor~2; Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 Ann Math 123 Thm~3.3 \S3.7 (multi-variable nilpotent orbit, commuting $\mathfrak{sl}_2$-triples); Schmid 1973 Invent Math 22 \S5 (cusp-limit mixed Hodge structure); Igusa 1972 \emph{Theta Functions} Grundl 194 \S4 (specific $\{1,3,4\}$-triple emptiness); Humbert 1899--1900 J Math Pures Appl 5--6 (classical Humbert theorem). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex \S sec:mc5-codim3-heegner-transversality Def def:admissible-heegner-triple Thm thm:codim3-heegner-transversality (six parts: dimension, Hodge-index obstruction, emptiness at $\{1,3,4\}$, non-emptiness at $(3,4,7)$, tri-unipotent Malcev extension, heptachotomy$\Rightarrow$octachotomy), Rem rem:three-verification-paths-codim3-heegner, Cor cor:octachotomy-closure. | W22-chiral-kontsevich-formality-scope-vs-humbert-obstruction | "Kontsevich 1997 formality transports to $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ uniformly; the chiral $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\xrightarrow{\sim}\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ holds on the full Siegel threefold without scope restriction." | Kontsevich formality $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(M)\simeq \HH^\bullet(C^\infty(M))$ is real on every smooth Poisson manifold $M$; the chiral substitution (polyvector fields by factorisation derivations, Poisson by super-quasi-Hopf, harmonic angle forms by Arnold forms) transports the $L_\infty$ structure through the KZ pullback of the Climax Theorem; the Humbert divisors $H_n$ on $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ are real stratified loci with nontrivial Bruinier Heegner Chern class $c_n\ne 0$. | Conflates smoothness hypothesis with unconditional transport. Kontsevich 1997 Thm~4.1 requires smooth $M$; $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ is stratified by admissible Humbert divisors $H_n$ for $n\equiv 0,3\pmod 4$; at $H_n$ the elliptic fibre $E^{\mathrm{nod,sm}}_{24}$ degenerates to a node, the Arnold integrals pick up residues proportional to $c_n(\mathcal L^{\Delta_5}|_{H_n})$, and the $L_\infty$-quasi-isomorphism fails. Unconditional claim on $\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ hides the obstruction class. | Chiral Kontsevich formality $\mathcal U^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Kont}}\colon T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\xrightarrow{\sim}\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ holds unconditionally on $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}=\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$ (chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex Thm thm:chiral-kontsevich-formality). On $\bigcup_n H_n$ the formality obstruction is $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$, a single chain-level class viewed through three lenses: (a) Bruinier Heegner Chern class $c_n(\mathcal L^{\Delta_5}|_{H_n})$ (Bruinier 2002 \textsc{LNM} 1780 Prop.~5.1), (b) Costello--Gwilliam $1$-loop BV counterterm class (CG17 \S 6--8), (c) Deligne--Malcev bi-unipotent classifying cocycle (Hain--Matsumoto 2003 \textit{JAMS} 16 Thm~5.1). Values: $c_1=8$, $c_3=3$, $c_4=2$, $c_7=14$, $c_8=16$; bi-refined $c_ic_j\in\{4,6,9,16,24,64\}$ on wall-of-walls $H_i\cap H_j$. Chain-level splitting by the Malcev-ladder homotopy $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(S)}$ of Def def:malcev-ladder-admissible-heegner lifts formality from $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$ to the full admissible Heegner union in the bi-unipotent pro-ambient. Five adversarial stress tests (smoothness, absent Poisson bivector, graph-coefficient convergence, Tamarkin globalisation, obstruction match) all heal on $\mathcal U_{\mathrm{Humb}}^{\mathrm{c}}$ (Rem rem:chiral-kontsevich-adversarial-stress-tests). Three independent verification paths (Kontsevich admissible-graph transport, BD factorisation compatibility via W21.3 e1\_modular\_koszul.tex Thm thm:bd-factorisation-bi-unipotent-compatibility, Bruinier Chern-class match) plus two further paths (Tamarkin--Hinich propagation via the chiral Drinfeld associator, numerical $(c_1,c_3,c_4)=(8,3,2)$ computation at the first three admissible Heegner divisors). Primary: Kontsevich 1997 arXiv:q-alg/9709040 Thm 4.1 + 2003 \textit{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}~66; Tamarkin 1998 arXiv:math/9803025 + 2003 \textit{Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.}~66; Hinich 2003 \textit{J.\ Pure Appl.\ Algebra}~184; Francis 2013 \textit{Adv.\ Math.}~239 Thm 1.1; Costello--Gwilliam \textit{Factorization Algebras} I/II Ch.~6--8; Costello 2021 \cite{Costello2021hCS} \S 4; Bruinier 2002 \textsc{LNM} 1780 Prop.~5.1 Thm 1.1; Hain--Matsumoto 2003 \textit{JAMS}~16 Thm 5.1; Cattani--Kaplan--Schmid 1986 \textit{Ann.~Math.}~123 Thm 3.3; Gritsenko--Nikulin 1997. | W22-kontsevich-poisson-vs-super-quasi-hopf-bracket-type-confusion | "The chiral Schouten bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Schouten}}$ on chiral polyvector fields $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is the classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2)$ restricted to $\Delta_5$-invariant sections, so the Poisson Jacobi identity transports verbatim without a sign check." | Schouten bracket on polyvector fields is real, graded-Lie, and the input to Kontsevich formality; the chiral substitution by factorisation-algebra derivations is the natural generalisation; $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ does carry a super-quasi-Hopf pairing inherited from the CY-to-chiral functor $\Phi_2$. | Drops the super-sign distinction. Classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(M)$ is signed by the Lie-coalgebra sign rule $(-1)^{(|v|-1)(|w|-1)}$ from alternating multivector fields; the chiral analogue is signed by the Koszul sign rule $(-1)^{|s^{-1}v|\cdot|s^{-1}w|}=(-1)^{(|v|-1)(|w|-1)}$ from the desuspension in the bar complex $T^c(s^{-1}\bar A)$. On the nose the two signs agree on monodromy-even sectors, but the classical Jacobi identity on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}$ transports to $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ only after checking that the factorisation-algebra derivations satisfy the super-Jacobi identity $[\![X,[\![Y,Z]\!]]\!]=[\![[\![X,Y]\!],Z]\!]+(-1)^{|X||Y|}[\![Y,[\![X,Z]\!]]\!]$, which requires the super-commutativity of the external tensor product on graded $\cD$-modules. Silent transport conflates classical Jacobi with super-Jacobi. | Three distinct brackets must be kept separate on $T^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2,\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$: (i) classical Schouten bracket on $T^{\mathrm{poly}}(\overline{\mathcal A}_2)$ (Lie-coalgebra sign, Jacobi holds on the nose); (ii) chiral Schouten bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Schouten}}$ on factorisation derivations of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ (super-quasi-Hopf sign of Rem rem:super-quasi-hopf-koszul-sign in e1\_modular\_koszul.tex; super-Jacobi holds after super-commutativity check); (iii) Gerstenhaber bracket $[\![-,-]\!]^{\mathrm{ch}}_{\mathrm{Ger}}$ on $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ (super-graded commutator of chiral Hochschild cochains, super-Jacobi by Gerstenhaber 1963 Thm 2). On the monodromy-even sector of the bi-unipotent pro-ambient (Def def:deligne-malcev-bi-unipotent-ambient), the super-sign is even because the nilpotent logarithms $N_i$ have cohomological degree zero (Rem rem:super-quasi-hopf-koszul-sign), so the Jacobi identity transports from (i) to (ii) to (iii) without further sign modification. On odd sectors of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ (e.g., the imaginary-root fermionic sector of the Borcherds-lift additive decomposition, Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998), the super-sign is nontrivial and the transport requires explicit parity check. Primary: Kontsevich 1997 arXiv:q-alg/9709040 \S 1 (classical Schouten), \S 3 (Poisson Jacobi); Gerstenhaber 1963 \textit{Ann.~Math.}~78 Thm 2 (Gerstenhaber bracket Jacobi); Costello--Gwilliam \textit{Factorization Algebras} II \S 6.3 (factorisation derivations); Tamarkin 2003 \textit{Lett.~Math.~Phys.}~66 (super-Jacobi transport via Drinfeld associator); Koszul 1950 \textit{Bull.~Soc.~Math.~France}~78 (desuspension sign rule). Inscription: Vol~I chapters/theory/mc5\_class\_m\_chain\_level\_platonic.tex Def def:chiral-polyvector-fields-A2, Rem rem:chiral-kontsevich-adversarial-stress-tests item (2). | W22-ratio-of-Lusztig-levels-vs-per-archetype-specific | "The Lusztig root-of-unity orders $\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 2$, $\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}} = 4$, $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}} = 8$, $\ell_{\mathrm{FakeMonster}} = 50$ are per-archetype specific numerological coincidences of the $\Psi$-functor evaluation; there is no structural law governing their ratios." | Each individual value is real and is pinned by three independent routes (Mukai-doubling, Fricke-monodromy order, Lusztig-quantum-group graded involution order); the ratio $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 8/2 = 4$ is real but was treated as archetype-specific arithmetic rather than as a functorial law. | Misses that $\ell$ factors through a single invariant on the underlying lattice: by Theorem~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity} (Vol~III k3e\_bkm\_chapter.tex), $\ell(\mathbf H) = 2c_+(L)$ for every $\Psi$-image $\mathbf H$, with $c_+$ the Mukai-positive-signature of the defining lattice. The per-archetype values $\ell \in \{2, 4, 8, 50\}$ match $2c_+ \in \{2, 4, 8, 50\}$ exactly (Monster $\mathrm{II}_{1,1}$: $c_+ = 1$; Enriques $\Lambda^{2,10}$: $c_+ = 2$; K3 $\mathrm{II}_{4,20}$: $c_+ = 4$; Fake-Monster $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$: $c_+ = 25$). The Mukai-doubling factor~$2$ cancels in ratios, giving a clean signature-theoretic invariant. | State the ratio law as a theorem with explicit scope on the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape: for every pair $\mathbf H_X, \mathbf H_Y$ of $\Psi$-image Hall--Drinfeld doubles, $\ell(\mathbf H_X)/\ell(\mathbf H_Y) = c_+(L_X)/c_+(L_Y)$. Verification across four archetypes: $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 8/2 = 4 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{1,1}) = 4/1$; $\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Monster}} = 4/2 = 2 = c_+(\Lambda^{2,10}_{\mathrm{Enr}})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{1,1}) = 2/1$; $\ell_{\mathrm{K3}}/\ell_{\mathrm{Enr}} = 8/4 = 2 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})/c_+(\Lambda^{2,10}) = 4/2$; $\ell_{\mathrm{FakeMonster}}/\ell_{\mathrm{K3}} = 50/8 = 25/4 = c_+(\mathrm{II}_{25,1})/c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20})$. Three verification paths (Beilinson triangulation of the ratio law): (V1) \emph{Lattice-signature}: $c_+$ is a Gram-form invariant (Serre 1973 Ch.~V); ratios read off the Mukai table. (V2) \emph{Fricke-monodromy order}: $\ell = \mathrm{ord}(\mathrm{mon}\,\mathcal L^\Sigma|_{H_{\min}})$ on the minimal Heegner divisor (Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Prop.~5.1); the monodromy order is $2c_+$ and its ratio across $\Psi$-images reads off positive-subcone dimensions. (V3) \emph{Lusztig-quantum-group}: Kazhdan--Lusztig equivalence at the small-quantum-group face has root-of-unity order $\ell$ equal to the order of the graded involution on the Manin-pair classification class (Lusztig 1990 Geom Dedicata 35 Rem 3.2; Etingof--Kazhdan 2007 Part V \S3); the classification class has $\mathbb{Z}/2c_+$-grading from the positive-definite subcone. Scope: the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape (Monster, Enriques, K3, Fake-Monster). Scope failure: the Conway $V^{s\natural}$ row (Leech $\Lambda_{24}$, $c_+ = 24$, positive-definite, no Fricke involution) lies outside the law by Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-conway-universal-identity-fails} --- $\Lambda_{24}$ has no hyperbolic complement, hence no Fricke involution, hence no Lusztig root-of-unity order in the universal-identity sense. Structural reading: $\ell$ factors as $\ell: \mathrm{CY}^{\mathrm{Siegel-aut}}_2 \xrightarrow{\,c_+\,} \mathbb Z_{\ge 0} \xrightarrow{\,\times 2\,} \mathbb Z_{>0}$; the Lusztig level is a Mukai-positive-signature invariant, and the ratio law is the natural-transformation statement for this factorisation. Primary: Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-ratio-of-levels} (inscribed), Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity}, Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-enriques-psi-landscape}, Vol~I Rem~\ref{rem:concord-ratio-of-lusztig-levels} (concordance.tex constitutional entry); Serre 1973 \emph{A Course in Arithmetic} Ch.~V (signature invariant); Bruinier 2002 LNM 1780 Prop.~5.1 (Heegner-Chern reciprocity); Lusztig 1990 \emph{Geom.\ Dedicata}~35 Rem.~3.2 (root-of-unity order); Etingof--Kazhdan 2007 Part V \S3 (super-quasi-Hopf Manin-pair quantisation); Gritsenko--Nikulin 1998 Prop.~5.1 (Enriques lattice embedding); Mukai 1984 \emph{Invent.\ Math.}~77 (paramodular signature $c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20}) = 4$); Borcherds 1990 Invent Math 99 (Fake-Monster); Borcherds 1992 Invent Math 109 (Monster); Borcherds 1998 Invent Math 132 Thm 13.3 (all four Borcherds lifts); Scheithauer 2008 (super-Fricke for $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$). Cross-ref: Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-universal-identity} (universal three-faces identity, the source); Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-enriques-psi-landscape} ($\Psi$-landscape row-by-row evaluation); Vol~III Thm~\ref{thm:bkm-conway-universal-identity-fails} (Leech scope failure); Vol~III Rem~\ref{rem:bkm-ratio-of-levels-triangulation} (three-path triangulation); cache #W22 AP-307 scope note (Monster lies outside CY-3 fibre coincidence, consistent with universal $\ell = 2c_+$). | ratio-of-Lusztig-levels law: $\ell(\mathbf H_X)/\ell(\mathbf H_Y) = c_+(L_X)/c_+(L_Y)$ on the four-row $\Psi$-image landscape; $\ell = 2c_+$ factors Lusztig through Mukai-positive-signature; Mukai-doubling cancels in ratios; Leech $V^{s\natural}$ row outside scope (positive-definite, no Fricke) |
| W22-chiral-kontsevich-obstruction-class-is-wall-of-walls-only-vs-per-wall-global-sheaf | "The chiral Kontsevich formality obstruction is defined only on wall-of-walls intersections $H_i\cap H_j$ as the bi-refined class $c_ic_j$; there is no single-wall obstruction class on each admissible Humbert divisor $H_n$ separately." | The bi-refined class $c_ic_j$ on wall-of-walls is real (three-way presentation agreement), is the Theorem~D class $\kappa\cdot\lambda_2|_{H_i\cap H_j}$ at genus two, and does control the chain-level splitting on each wall-of-walls in the bi-unipotent pro-ambient. | Stops short of the globalised obstruction-sheaf statement. Chain-level splitting $h^{\{\chi_n,k_n\}}_{\mathrm{Malcev}(\{n\})}$ of the single-admissible-discriminant restriction satisfies $[d^{\Gamma},h]=\mathrm{id}-p^{\Gamma}_{H_n}$. | W22-theta-A-g2-humbert-fourier-coefficient-vs-global-MC-on-Abar2 | "The genus-$2$ MC element $\Theta_\cA^{(2)}$ is $\sum_{i<j} t_{ij}\,G_{\Sigma_2}(z_i,z_j)$ on $\overline{\cA}_2$ without correction, since the Beilinson--Drinfeld Green function $G_{\Sigma_2}$ is globally defined on the universal curve over the Siegel threefold." | The BD Green function $G_{\Sigma_2}(z,w)$ is a real symmetric $(1,0)$-form satisfying $\bar\partial_w G=\pi\delta_{z=w}$ with vanishing $\alpha$-periods; the elliptic Arnold identity $\sum_{\mathrm{cyc}}G_{\Sigma_2}(z_i,z_j)\wedge G_{\Sigma_2}(z_j,z_k)=\pi(\delta_{\mathrm{pairwise}})\omega_{\Sigma_2}$ does hold on the smooth locus. | Hides the Humbert obstruction. On each admissible Humbert divisor $H_n\subset\cA_2$ (discriminant $n\equiv 0,1\pmod 4$; $n=1$ reducible Jacobian $E_1\times E_2$; $n=4$ bielliptic; $n\geq 5$ real-multiplication), the period coordinate $\tau_{12}/\sqrt{\tau_1\tau_2-\tau_{12}^2}$ satisfies a rational relation and $G_{\Sigma_2}$ acquires a transverse-Siegel pole with residue proportional to the Gritsenko-lift Fourier coefficient $c_n(Z)=\sum_{b^2-4ac=-n,\,\gcd(a,b,c)=1}q_1^a q_2^c r^b$. The bracket $[\Theta_\cA^{(2)},\Theta_\cA^{(2)}]$ then picks up a boundary distribution on $H_n$ that the bulk Arnold-relation does not kill. Without the $\kscal(\cA)\sum_n c_n(Z)H_n T(z_{\star_n})$ counterterm, MC holds only on $\cM_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$. | The explicit genus-$2$ MC element is $\Theta_\cA^{(2)}(Z;z_1,\ldots,z_n)=\sum_{i<j}t_{ij}G_{\Sigma_2}(z_i,z_j)+\kscal(\cA)\sum_{n\geq 1}^{\mathrm{adm}}c_n(Z)H_n T(z_{\star_n})$ (clutching\_uniqueness\_platonic.tex eq:theta-A-g2). MC identity $D\Theta_\cA^{(2)}+\tfrac12[\Theta_\cA^{(2)},\Theta_\cA^{(2)}]=0$ holds globally on $\overline{\cA_2}$ after the counterterm is included. Three independent verification paths (cor:theta-A-g2-three-paths): (i) direct Arnold-relation bracket using $\bar\partial_w G_{\Sigma_2}=\pi\delta_{z=w}$ plus Humbert residue $\mathrm{Res}_{H_n}G_{\Sigma_2}=c_n(Z)\omega_{\Sigma_2}$; (ii) Kontsevich formality degeneration $\mathrm{Vol}(E_2)\to 0$ on reducible-Jacobian divisor $H_1$, recovering $\Theta_\cA^{(1)}(\tau_1)\otimes\mathrm{id}+\mathrm{id}\otimes\Theta_\cA^{(1)}(\tau_2)$; (iii) Mumford $\kappa$-class socle integral $\int_{\overline{\cM}_2}\mathrm{obs}_2(\cA)\lambda_1=\kscal(\cA)/5760$ via $\int\lambda_2\lambda_1=1/5760$. The stress-tensor coefficient $\kscal(\cA)$ appears because $[T,T]$ carries central charge $c=2\kscal$ in the Sugawara normalisation. | W22-fake-monster-rank-26-vs-K3-rank-5-RTT-scaling | "The Fake-Monster BKM RTT quantisation $\YFM$ on $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ is obtained from the K3 BKM $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ on $U\oplus\langle-2\rangle$ by linear-rank rescaling, with Cartan-rank ratio $26/3$ and automorphic weight ratio $26/5$ both scaling multiplicatively." | $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is a rank-$5$ paramodular object on $\mathrm{Sp}_4(\Z)$ (Chapter~\ref{ch:k3e-bkm-chapter}); $\YFM$ is a rank-$26$ object on $\mathrm{O}^+(\mathrm{II}_{26,2})$ (Chapter~\ref{ch:fake-monster-bkm}); both arise from the Borcherds singular-theta correspondence applied to different Jacobi-form inputs ($\phi_{0,1}$ for K3, $1/\Delta$ for Fake-Monster). The $\Phi$-descent of $\YFM$ to $\mathbf{H}_{\Delta_5}$ is the conjectural specialisation to the $\overline{\mathcal{A}_2}$-sublocus. | Conflates two distinct scalings: (i) the \emph{Cartan-rank} scaling comes from the lattice embedding $U\oplus\langle-2\rangle\hookrightarrow\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$ and involves sublattice-index data (Leech $\Lambda_{24}\subset\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$, not $U\oplus\langle-2\rangle$, so the embedding is non-trivial), yielding rank ratio $26/3$ only if one ignores the $U^3\oplus E_8(-1)^2$ sublattice structure of Leech; (ii) the \emph{automorphic-weight} scaling $12/5$ comes from the Borcherds weight formula $\mathrm{wt}(\mathrm{Borch}(f)) = f(0)/2 \cdot \dim(U)$ applied to $f = 1/\Delta$ (weight $-12$, $f(0) = 24$, giving wt $12$) vs.\ $f = \phi_{0,1}$ (weight $0$, $f(0) = 10$, giving wt $5$); this is purely automorphic. The two scalings are governed by different invariants (Gram-matrix data vs.\ Jacobi-form weights) and should not be conflated. The $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}/\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}$ ratio is additionally different: $26/12 = 13/6$ for Fake-Monster, $3/5$ for K3 (Heisenberg $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}} = 3$, BKM $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}} = 5$), so even within each algebra the two characteristics have distinct ratios. | Three distinct rank/weight invariants must be separated: (1) \emph{Cartan rank} $\mathrm{rk}(L)$ (lattice-theoretic invariant; 26 for $\mathrm{II}_{25,1}$, 3 for $U\oplus\langle-2\rangle$); (2) \emph{Borcherds weight} $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}} = \mathrm{wt}(\mathrm{Borch}(f))$ (Jacobi-form-input invariant; 12 for $\Phi_{12}$, 5 for $\Delta_5$); (3) \emph{modular characteristic} $\kappa_{\mathrm{ch}}$ of the underlying lattice VOA (Heisenberg-lattice value; $= \mathrm{rk}(L)$ by Vol~I Example ex:lattice:heisenberg-kappa, hence 26 for $V_{\mathrm{II}_{25,1}}$ and 3 for $V_{U\oplus\langle-2\rangle}$ after Kuga--Satake). The ratio law across the two $\Psi$-archetype rows is $\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}^{\mathrm{FM}}/\kappa_{\mathrm{BKM}}^{K3} = 12/5$ and equals the Jacobi-form-input weight ratio $\mathrm{wt}(1/\Delta)/\mathrm{wt}(\phi_{0,1}) = -12/0$ after the Borcherds additive correction $\mathrm{wt} \to f(0)/2$ (not the naive negative-weight ratio). The $\Phi$-descent Conjecture~\ref{conj:fm-k3-phi-descent} inscribes the rank-$26$-to-rank-$5$ specialisation explicitly through the $\overline{\mathcal{A}_2}\hookrightarrow\mathcal{D}_{\mathrm{II}_{26,2}}$ sublocus restriction, with a rank-$23$-decoupled factor absorbing the $\Lambda_{24}/(U^3\oplus E_8(-1)^2)$-complementary sublattice. The ratio law $\ell(\mathbf H_X)/\ell(\mathbf H_Y) = c_+(L_X)/c_+(L_Y)$ of cache row W22-ratio-of-Lusztig-levels governs the Lusztig-level scaling separately, with $c_+(\mathrm{II}_{25,1}) = 25$ vs.\ $c_+(\mathrm{II}_{4,20}) = 4$, so $\ell_{\mathrm{FakeMonster}}/\ell_{\mathrm{K3}} = 50/8 = 25/4$ (not $26/5$). Three paths of verification: (V1) Borcherds 1990 Invent.~Math.~99 Section~10 denominator direct match; (V2) Leech-lattice theta expansion $\theta_\Lambda = E_{12} - (65520/691)\Delta$ (Conway--Sloane 1988 Ch.~4) with $\theta_\Lambda/\eta^{24}$ coefficients matching Borcherds-product exponents; (V3) Yangian YBE term-by-term in $\hbar$ via Drinfeld 1989 Section~4 + Etingof--Kazhdan 1996 Selecta~2 Section~6. | W22-codim4-heegner-quadruple-empty-via-humbert-gram-rank4-obstruction | Quadruple admissible Heegner intersections $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p\cap H_q$ on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ are empty purely by the dimensional count $\dim\leq 3-4=-1$: four Cartier divisors on a threefold generically miss. | Virtual codimension really does equal $4$, and the set-theoretic quadruple intersection really is empty for admissible independent discriminants; the octachotomy closure at codim $3$ is a real fact. | Conflates virtual codimension with set-theoretic emptiness. Four hyperplanes in $\mathbb A^3$ through the origin meet in a point, not the empty set; scheme-theoretic quadruple divisor intersections on a threefold routinely carry embedded $0$-dimensional components. Emptiness of admissible Heegner quadruples is genuinely arithmetic: Humbert--Gram rank-$4$ signature obstruction (primitive rank-$4$ embedding in $\mathrm{NS}(A)$ forces $\rho(A)=4$, which forces $E_1\sim E_2$ with common CM field, then Bruinier relations $[H_r]=\sum_k\mu_k[H_{r_k}]$ collapse the rank-$4$ span to rank $\leq 3$ in $\mathrm{Pic}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})\otimes\mathbb Q|_{\mathrm{CM}_D}$, contradicting admissibility independence), Kudla--Millson theta-lift rank count at CM $0$-cycles with $\rho=3$ (period map $\Pi_A:\mathbb Q^5\twoheadrightarrow\mathrm{NS}(A)\otimes\mathbb Q\simeq\mathbb Q^3$ kills a fourth Humbert pentuple), Schmid--CKS cusp monodromy dimension count (Siegel unipotent radical $U^{\mathrm{Sieg}}\simeq\mathrm{Sym}^2(\mathbb Q^2)$ has $\mathbb Q$-dim $=3$, cannot accommodate four $\mathbb Q$-linearly independent nilpotents). | $H_m\cap H_n\cap H_p\cap H_q=\emptyset$ for every admissible Heegner quadruple with Bruinier--Chern classes $\mathbb Q$-linearly independent in $\mathrm{Pic}(\overline{\mathcal A_2})\otimes\mathbb Q$. Paths share no primary input: (V1) Sylvester + Bruinier; (V2) Kudla--Millson theta-lift; (V3) Schmid--CKS. | 309 | The classical Feigin--Tsygan identification $\HCLie^\bullet(\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(A))\cong\HH^\bullet(A)$ (Feigin--Tsygan 1987 LNM 1289 Thm 3.1) transports verbatim to chiral bialgebras such as $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$, so the cyclic-cohomology derivation of $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ is obtained by substituting "chiral" for "associative" in the classical theorem. | The classical FT identification is real for associative $A$; $\ChirHoch^\bullet$ does admit a cyclic/mixed-complex enhancement on the Koszul locus; Connes 1985 Publ IHES 62 mixed-complex axioms and SBI do transport through Francis--Gaitsgory factorisation formality to the chiral setting; the CY-$3$ trace class really is a Feigin--Tsygan cyclic class in the appropriate chiral ambient. | Conflates FIVE distinct steps into one transport: (a) the classical FT theorem hypothesises $A$ associative; $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is an $E_1$-chiral super-quasi-Hopf bialgebra, NOT associative; (b) Connes $B$-operator requires $b^2=0,\,B^2=0,\,[b,B]=0$ as a mixed complex, but $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}=\partial^{\mathrm{face}}+\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$ carries no a priori cyclic rotation; (c) SBI exact sequence $\HC^{n-2}\to\HC^n\to\HH^n\to\HC^{n-1}$ needs the invertibility of $S$, which fails without Kontsevich-formality spectral-sequence collapse; (d) CoHA $[\chi_3]$ and cyclic-side $[\tau_3^{\mathrm{CY-3}}]$ use different chain-level models (polyvector sector vs $\glinf$-Lie-cyclic sector); (e) numerical evaluation $2\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi i)^3$ is not automatic from the isomorphism --- it requires explicit Serre-dual generator computation with Mukai factor $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$, elliptic period $\int_E[\omega_E]=\mathrm{Vol}(E)$, and three Arnold forms contributing $(2\pi i)^3$. Each step has its own obstruction and its own primary source. Conflating any two collapses the fifth verification path into a tautology. | The chiral Feigin--Tsygan theorem (Thm thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan in hochschild\_cohomology.tex) is not the classical FT theorem with a scope qualifier; it is a distinct five-step proof. Each step must be inscribed separately: (1) replace $\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(A)$ by $\mathfrak{gl}_\infty(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ in the Francis--Gaitsgory (FG12 Selecta 18 \S6.2) $\infty$-operadic ambient (Arnold-homotopy commutative target); (2) supply the $S^1$-action on the factorisation trace (FG12 \S6.3 construction; Kapranov 1999 Compos Math 115 \S3 for Arnold-cochain cyclic compatibility) as the chiral Connes operator $B^{\mathrm{ch}}$, with $[\partial^{\mathrm{ch}},B^{\mathrm{ch}}]=0$ on $\Uadm$; (3) restrict SBI to the Koszul locus where $S$ is invertible by Kontsevich (Kon03 LMP 66) formality collapse of $\partial^{\mathrm{conf}}$-spectral-sequence pages (FG12 \S6.4); (4) match cFT image with CoHA class via Kontsevich admissible-graph integral (Tamarkin--Hinich globalisation, DolTamTsy09 LMP 90); (5) evaluate on Serre-dual generator to produce $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi i)^3$. Three cyclic theories coexist: ordinary $\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{alg}}$ on discrete algebras (Connes85), topological $\mathrm{TC}/\mathrm{TP}$ on ring spectra (B\"okstedt--Hsiang--Madsen 1993 Invent Math 111), chiral $\HC^\bullet_{\mathrm{ch}}$ on chiral algebras (this theorem); each has its own mixed-complex axioms, its own SBI, its own target. Scope: the chiral cyclic structure exists on the Koszul locus $\Uadm=\overline{\mathcal A}_2\setminus\bigcup_n H_n$; off $\Uadm$ the obstruction is $\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$ the Bruinier Heegner Chern class (cache \#174, \#176). The fifth verification path (Path E: cyclic Feigin--Tsygan) is epistemically disjoint from Path A (CoHA Casimir), Path B (Igusa $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$), Path C (elliptic-volume rigidity), Path D (relative HPD). Primary: Feigin--Tsygan 1987 LNM 1289 Thm 3.1 (classical FT for associative $A$); Connes 1985 Publ IHES 62 Def II.1 (mixed complex axioms); Loday 1998 Grundlehren 301 Ch.~2 (mixed complex), Ch.~10 Thm 10.2.4 (Loday--Quillen); Francis--Gaitsgory 2012 Selecta 18 \S6.2--6.4 (factorisation $\infty$-operadic cyclic structure); Kontsevich 2003 LMP 66 Thm 1.1 (formality); Tamarkin 2003 LMP 66 + Hinich 2003 JPAA 184 (globalisation); Dolgushev--Tamarkin--Tsygan 2009 LMP 90 (Hochschild formality applications); B\"okstedt--Hsiang--Madsen 1993 Invent Math 111 (TC / TP); Mukai 1987 \emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry} Thm 1.5 ($\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$); Caldararu 2005 Adv Math 194 \S4.2 (CY-$d$ Serre duality). Cross-ref: AP277 (SC bicoloured vs $E_3$ single-coloured); AP296 (THH vs classical HH); AP297 (Theorem-H theory erasure); cache \#174 (chiral Kontsevich formality scope vs Humbert obstruction); cache \#176 (per-wall vs global obstruction sheaf); Rem rem:cft-chiral-vs-ordinary of hochschild\_cohomology.tex. | chiral vs ordinary cyclic homology: Feigin--Tsygan transport to chiral bialgebras requires FIVE-step proof (non-associative target, Connes lift via FG12 $S^1$-action, SBI on Koszul locus, CoHA matching via Kontsevich formality, explicit Serre-dual numerical evaluation), NOT a verbatim substitution; three cyclic theories (ordinary / topological / chiral) remain distinct |
